O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine by filling it with its contents, and have made its end through his explanations and by his declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to my vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is scarce in our region and is lacking in every detail, the science has perished and been cut away, and nothing remains except the small descriptions in books by the ancients that the hands have executed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came errors and vanities, and the intentions have been closed, and the science has been forsaken.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I should revitalize it all together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will bring together the forms of the cautery tools, and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation thereof, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it behooves him who undertakes this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he know the judgment of the members, their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and their movement and veins moving and at rest, and from what place they issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, Hippocrates said that the needle with the knot is much, and with the work is little; and especially in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We hereby state in the introduction to this book that whoever is not aware of the matters previously mentioned should take care lest he make a mistake and deceive people; thus, I have often wished that more of those who undertake this science and abandon their knowledge and experience would refrain from doing so.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who incised the abscess of scrofula or throat of a woman, and incised the arteries of her neck; therefore so much blood issued forth that the woman died in her own hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another surgeon who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; so he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to draw the stone, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and well knew that if he were cut he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another patient who was treating the duke of our land, who had a broken leg, and with the breaking instrument made a wound; and the doctors full of ignorance placed the break on the wound with strong ligatures, and left no part of the wound without salve, and left it thus until the end; and he commanded that he not displace it at all; and remained thus until the leg became completely swollen and the foot rotted away.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and hastened to come to free the leg; and when I heard it dislocate, he was at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways when corruption was already confirmed or member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to go through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And let another mirer collapse the anchored abscess, and then inflame it through the wickedness of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure melancholic humor, it does not matter to touch it with iron if it is in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear student, you need to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, those where there is danger in many positions. I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because it is necessary that you take care, so that the foolish may not speak ill of you. If you take your arms in counsel, and undertake your sick lightly and firmly, and use the best way so by the grace of God you come to salvation and be joyful; and leave the fearful diseases of grief sanity; and remove your arms from those who cause you doubt, and have faith in them that you may go from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galien says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a false disease, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have discussed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and water-cautery medicines, and the chapters are ordered from the head down to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the metal tools for cautery, and everything necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and about suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about resetting dislocations and twists, and similar things; and are ordered from the head down to the feet, with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, as we recall the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of the aid and of the harm, are the longest discourse and subtle science and the secret answers; and about these many wise ones spoke, and agreed with them; and their words suffice me little, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery aids universally in all temperaments where there is matter; for there are two temperaments: namely, hot temperament due to matter, and dry temperament due to matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry temperament with matter, some discussed and said that the fire cautery is great aid; and others said the opposite: that the fire cautery is not useful for diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat diseases that are already hot or dry; and those who say the opposite state that the fire cautery does great aid to hot and dry diseases that affect the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true once by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And moreover, do not meddle with it except those who have proven it, and who know the chapter on cautery through long use, the diversity of the temperaments of men, their dispositions and causes of diseases, their symptoms and the space of time; we have no fear from other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the signs gathered and agreed with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery altogether with heat is of the secrets of treatments, and has greater goodness than a burning medicinal cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and only affects the part that is cauterized, and does not harm other parts little by little.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines that burn come from one part to another by diffusion, and cause diseases in other parts hindering healing; and by chance, the patient might die from the fire due to its intensity and the quality of its substance unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experiment and the long course of service and study I have devoted to the art, which is based on the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse the length of my words, as it pleases me not to deprive you of the secret that lies in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, when the fire cauteries should be performed, and they chose the times.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is suitable in all times, for the harm coming on is kept away by means of the cautery; and especially when the cautery is for pains urgent and necessary that cannot wait for the time until greater mischief arises in the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think so, dear son, as do the foolish doctors; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return. And they say thus: but it is not as they believe, for a cautery is merely medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is worthier than other medicines for its speed of effect and the virtue of its action and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes once according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its virtue; and in him are assembled superfluities through the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at the locus where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauterizations for teeth due to pain, and similar things, and then the pain does not return at all; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And few people understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauterizations work after medicine, and their intentions are false, for when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cauterization, and it does work.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is well known that cauterization is the latest in medicine, not according to the intention of wise men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizers of gold are more effective than iron ones, and they said this not because of the quality of gold or its high value; and they said that the blisters from a gold cautery do not cause putrefaction, but it is not true, for I have tested it and found that it does happen in some people; and cauterizers of gold are more effective than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And whenever you heat an instrument of gold, you must not leave it when it is hot by the color of the gold, and let it cool quickly; and if you heat it too much, put it in water; and thus there are enough precautions.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter from the head to the feet, because the veins shall be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold in the head, and there are two of them where we treat by the cause of a disease called "soda", and by the cause of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for the multitude of dreams and toothache and throat pain, and especially for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient must be purged by solutive medicine, changing the nature of the illness for three or four days, according to what the virtue and strength and custom of the ill person can bear; and then remove the head from the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place it crosswise between your hands, and put his hands on soft pillows; after that, put the root of your palm above the root of his nose between his two eyes; and let where your two means come, bleed from there. Then heat the cautery called "olivare," as its form is thus:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and do this by slowly lowering and extracting your hand little by little, turning it. Then withdraw your hand entirely, and probe the wound if you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. After that, take a little salt, and put in wet wool, and place it on the wound, and let it remain for three days. Afterwards, apply a moistened cloth with butter; leave it on until the scalding is removed. Finally, treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that when a wound remains open longer, it purges more; therefore, move it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of them said that the cautery must be applied such that part of the bone is burned, and then the burned part of the bone should be removed and cleaned.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the cautery should be applied so strongly as to burn a width as large as the ring that women wear in their noses, for this causes the humors to move out. One must keep the wound open long; afterward, one must clean and draw it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of applying the cautery do not seem to me to be good in all respects, except in some cases where there is fear. I believe that I should apply the lesser one; for the shoulder is weakened by continuous natural dislocations, as we testify in other limbs; and even when the patient's shoulder is weak by nature, and the first application of cautery seems more beneficial and less harmful to me, from this I work out this particular benefit.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of old pain from the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When pain in the head is chronic and lasts long, the patient should use medicines for a year and pills called "cochie," and treatments for purging the head and eyes and plasters; and if they are pricked with the cautery as we have previously said, it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take heed that the head of the sick person is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize beneath that cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each horn of the head down to the bone as we have said before, do the cautery over the vein called "vasselz"; and the vein is where one places the suction cups; and lighten your hand so that you do not go down to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries for the horns should be finer than those used for the middle part of the head, and this is their form.
dou cautere dou chief	for the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and the illness extends to the eye, and the head is purified by medicinal means, and other treatments have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then he makes cauteries according to two ways, that is to say with medicine ague and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with medicine ague is that you take a clove of garlic, and peel off the skin and part of the outer layer for just two heads. Then place it in the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can insert the garlic clove beneath the scalp; and when it is inserted, hold it tightly and leave it there for twelve hours; then remove it and apply a plaster with butter until it dries up. Leave the wound uncovered for two or three days; then place a cloth soaked in butter over the area.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment until he is healed; and if you see, then do those of some burning medicines that I have written or tenth treatise of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron cautery with coal to form it:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the tip is made in the shape of a bell with only a little projection, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and slightly move the iron gently, so that half the thickness of the heart's flesh is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is above, does not burn, and let plenty of blood flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After place cotton in readiness of a sieve, and put on the shoulder for three days; then place soft cotton bathed in butter, and thereafter treat the shoulder with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this inflammation with the cautery called "cultellare", do so at its point entirely, and beware of scarring the artery in this inflammation which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of inflammation
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat inflammation as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cautery and cauterization with iron are insufficient, then it is necessary to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white-hot; apply thusly over the painful area a line half a digit long, and withdraw your hand once, ensuring you do not scar the artery and do not reach the bone; beware of the mandible that moves when eating, and let the nerves have regard only to sensation and avoid spasms in the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or cutting with great fear and especially those who are not learned and inexperienced; leave the work half done; but I will tell you how one stops bleeding from an artery when it is cut, and I will show you where this occurs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery having two knives; and this cautery is better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division do not help, then heat this cautery called "poins," as its form is described here:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After piercing all around the affected ear, or in both places where the pain is felt, and then move slightly upwards from the root of the ear after having marked the spot; do ten points around each ear; afterwards cure the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by fire cautery is not of those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply fire cautery to similar cases that come from drying up and decay of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this condition of torture that moves from phlegm in the fluids, purgatives, and gargling, and if it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another slightly above the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and apply the cautery just above the top of the ear by a small distance from the tip of the ear, and another along the temple as long as an inch; let the cautery remain there until the middle part of the heart is burned; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the likeness of the cutaneous one that we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and it should be that the knives are a bit larger; after the cure of the head as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and the patient does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then I make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the head, and one on the neck which is called "vassels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and cure them as we have said before.
de litargie	of lithargyrium
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is fitting to give the patient great and purifying yeres and pills for the brain; after cleansing the head of the patient thoroughly, place on the occiput the sinapism plaster as written or treated in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of the cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed thus, well and good; and if it is not, perform three cauteries descending from the head down to the neck, with a large space between each cautery. Cure it as for the others, and if you see fit, and the patient suffers, do the third cautery in the middle; and when necessary, two more above the two horns, and cure until it is healed; let the cauteries be called "olive," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of dandruff and of what we have said before; then touch the patient's head, afterward make a fire cautery between the head and on each horn, behind and three above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering greatly, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries above the spine of the back; and leave them until the deeper part is burned, then lift your hand; afterward treat the burns until they are healed, and let it be the cautery called "olive" which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use fire cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to cleanse the brain of dandruff and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patients are great and suffer from cold medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if this is an infant who cannot tolerate the pain, make them gargle and chew with modifications to the brain often using good meats; after placing the head in the middle, and I apply the fire cautery as we have said before, on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffering, I apply cauteries as I said for those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the olive cauteries be according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, apply the fire cautery with subtlety according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the superfluities or corrupted moisture are thick and large, then apply the fire cautery of such cauteries as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities decline to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then he should drink something by which his brain may be cleansed, according to what was said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After heating the shoulder of the patient; after making the linen well, as a circle, so place it under the shoulder; and the patient should lie crossed, and be well held from all sides; after presenting the liniment, and value much of butter of barberry ancient; and the heated one by fire tempered, that the dough can on his applying can suffer; after emptying the circle from within under the shoulder, and let it cool; and do this to the patient each week once with another good government, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see cauterization done by making several pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the brain more; and then put on damp cotton soaked in butter and gelatin grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the awe of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awe comes first to the eyes through the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and cause the patient to drink purifying things for the head, and keep them away from all moisture, and make them sweat or have baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After this, instruct them to bend their head backward, and cauterize through the head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the descent of awe is to both eyes together, or in one if the descent is in one. And cover the entire cauterization with all the veins and arteries beneath the heart, making the cauterizations long according to the width of the temple; and guard against the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood come out, stop it as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incision how to handle it; and sometimes one makes a fire cautery or hot iron over the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the heart the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins, or detract from the arteries that appear at the front of the head; and one sees that they are cold phlegmatic superfluities, then I make the cautery that I said at the beginning of this work descending to the eyes: I cautere over the forehead, two cauteries over the temples, and two cauteries or hot irons over the two rear bones; and if there is more need, I cauterize saignement above the sorcil with all the small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from the body through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not profit at all, then let the patient drink three nosegays; after that, lance the head, and do a cautery or in the middle of the olive oil cautery; and do two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two sorics, a bit below the hairline; and beware of the artery so you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil becomes softened due to illness and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which here is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you must make two cauteries on the two sinews as long as the evil spirits are; and do not leave the hand aside until the third part of the paper be burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair which points to the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes the hairs of the eyes turn white and prick the eye, and in such cases cauteries are applied according to two methods: that is, by fire, or with a burning medicinal substance.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are equal, then place the patient in good health; after that, draw a figure on the paper of the eye as is like the leaf of the laurel, and let it be the beginning of the sign among the hairs; then put moistened cotton in egg white and myrrh on the eye, then heat the cautery as its form is described.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you have drawn several times very little at a time, until the eyes are scorched in place; and the signs of health of the work are that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the outline of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave thus for three days, after which put moistened cotton in butter until the scalding is removed; afterwards apply ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs come and the paper is softened, then resume the cautery on that same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are thin, cauterize until the paper is lifted to its natural place, and is even, and do not prick the hair near the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even. Then take parchment and make its shape like the leaf of bay; then take French soap and strong heat, one drachm of each, and grind them well together; and apply it quickly, so that it does not cool, over the form you have made as the shape of the bay leaf, and put eyes on the paper. And if the disease is only in the eye, open only I, and if in both also; and put wet cotton under the eye soaked in egg white; and the patient's head be in a normal position and place your finger showing over the medicine, and press it slightly and the eyelid every time the patient feels the medicine biting, for he feels the bite as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your duty.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite has passed, lift the eyelid and reward if you see the paper lifted as if it were lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, put the medicine again on the eyelid or where the medicine has not acted, as long as your actions are equal, and your eyes placed steadily; then put a wet cloth with butter on it until the pain is gone, after which cure the eyelid of the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to guard your work well with great care so that the medicine does not stick to the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft later, and the hairs prick in the eye, restart the treatment on that side which is softened by the paper properly, as you have done before; after the wound heals; and this is the form of the leaf of the myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that men's eyes are different in size and smallness, and according to this, your constraints; and do not always direct the right way to him for whom this art is studied.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by fire cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head on your shoulder; and guide the minister's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move and does not shift from its position; afterwards, put moist cotton in the yolk of an egg or in persillion juice over the eye; afterwards heat the cautery which is divided: and place it on the head as if forming a pen of a woodpecker, together with which the cautery should be; if you see, make it point from one head to another, and if you see, make it also like a tent; but in any case, what is placed there must move for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After this, if the fistula is open, drain the pus and dry it; and if it is closed, work on it, and draw out the bow (likely a term for a foreign body). Afterwards, place the hot cautery in the form of a cone, and hold your hand at the part above the neck under the eye to prevent your hand from doing mischief. Place the cautery in the oil's fat, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, begin the cautery again once more, and do so as often as you need, and let it be for three days; after that, put on moist cotton with butter, and the treatment of the drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, apply a watery corrosive medicine until the bone is revealed; then proceed according to what is in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Hear about the fistula, and make it clean; after that, place in the opening one slender thread of wool:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they do this to the quantity of one penny; and hold your hand or arm firmly, and let not the patient move at all, that the melted plonc does not run into his eye; and it is necessary to put on the eye of the patient wet wool in egg white or in ale: the plonc thus heals the fistula and the healthy part with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if not, it is necessary to administer pertusin to the nose, and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose according to what is proper in itself.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur in lips called "poil," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When the cure for these cracks, as we have said in the divisions, does not help, then heat the small fire cautery knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it in the cracks until it cools; afterwards, dress the wound with ointment until it heals.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or to the eye socket, or palate, or to the roots of the teeth, after putrefaction and is matured and becomes a fistula; then cure it as we have said in the divisions, but if it does not help: then you must use the cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards, plug or perforate the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron cools at the bottom of it, and behind it; and do this one or two times, after the cure as we have said in the treatments until it heals; and if it is cured thus, that is good; and if not, you must expose the wound and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	by movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and if treatment with medicines is ineffective, then put the patient's chief in your healthy one; afterwards, heat the cautery as described later in such a manner that you place a cane on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery into the tooth, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after that, remove your hand and continue with the cautery as you see fit; afterwards, fill the patient's mouth with salty water, let it sit for an hour, and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a manner, the tooth that was moving is stabilized, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of teeth comes from cold or there is cold present, and the treatments with medicines are ineffective, then it has need of cautery according to two ways: and cautery of wax and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of wax is such that you take wax from a cow, and melt it at the end of an iron or tin spoon; then take cotton and wrap it at the tip of a tent, and the moistened wax; and place it quickly on the painful tooth, holding until it cools down; and do this often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see soft wool and cotton in cooled wax, and place it on the painful tooth, and put hot iron on top until the fire reaches the pulp of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery of fire is such that you take one or more iron pins or nails, and let them be large enough that the flame does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, as will be described later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled; do this often, for the pain will be removed that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter in anticipation of the cautery, and then quickly apply it; this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And apply the cautery to whichever tooth you want, and according to what you have power to do; this is the form of the pin:
des scrophules	of the scrofulous glands
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulous glands are of phlegm and cold moisture, and do not yield to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery ember from which the form will come, and have two openings for the smoke to escape on the other side; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or as necessary until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it for three days; and place moist wax cloth on top until the burning is gone; after that, treat the wound with ointments and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cantharus:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures overcome the channels of the body, and especially when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first evacuated of fluids with solutive medicines; after which perform a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn the heart but only slightly.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After which perform another cautery at the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and let the cauteries be called "clavile" of which we have the form before; and cure it as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cauterization
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all diseases of the body are due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or drying, and the disease is old, then perform two cauteries on the flanks at their sides; and another cautery between the breasts; and let the cauteries be called "clavile" according to the form described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a fire cautery at the points where the cautery is called "points" of which the form was described earlier in the illness of the ears; and let there be the points up to 30, or around that number.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment of the head as previously described, let there be three fire cauteries according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And since these cautery marks are lighter, because you make three in one application.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After you have treated the patient on their back and side; afterwards, touch the heart within with your left hand at its ribs; and if the dislocation is out of place internally, heat the fire cautery which has two nooses formed.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it perceives pain up to the ribs, and bring together the figure of the cautery with four cauteries; and for this, a cautery with three nooses is made, because the figure of the cauterization consists of three cauteries; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery with three nooses.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted over this first nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After placing the cauterizer with powdered roots and salt; after this, let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, little happens, then cauterize over the thick part of the cautery clave, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach to such an extent as it is contrary to his constitution, and there are many catharrs in him, and by the usual methods of treatment they do not profit, then it must be treated on his back, and he should extend his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, I will make three cauteries on the inner side of the foot for the size of a coin, all the cauteries close to the heel, and two further down the two sides so that the shape of the cauteries is at three angles, and have space between them so that when they putrefy they do not be joined together; and let the cauteries be perfect so that they penetrate both parts of the heel, and the shape of the cauteries according to this form without alteration:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cautereze by pricking and bleeding above the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you see of inch; then cauterize all the cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we had before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes to pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, while it is forced out of its natural temperament due to superfluities; the patients are treated as we have said in divisions, and if they do not profit from it, then the patients must be treated on their side; and mark three cautery marks according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondria, where the ribs of man come; and let there be the width of a finger between each cautery mark; and may the cautery marks be as long as one's body, and do not press too much with your hand over the entire cautery mark; and be burned only the halves of the keur, and have the patient lie straight on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is so, cautereze these cauteries of the cuticular, being subtle and skillful in the art, and guard that you do not burn all the heart, for you would dry up all the body; and that it come not to a boil, for the hearts are most delicate there, and the wise ones to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too severe; and if it is in the membrane, the pain is intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment heals the membranes, it is necessary that the patient be treated at its source; and then scrape the flesh or abscess, and then heat the cautery which resembles fire, of which here is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And apply the fire cautery until the blisters form up to syphacia, until all the pustules are gone; after the cure, as in the treatment of poultices, until it is healed; and it must not be used any more than this cautery by those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at least once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may boldly operate, and always it seems to me that it is better to leave them alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the fire cautery of pleursin.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleursin cautery, one should use roots of angelica, and in this manner: take a long root of angelica, the largest you can find, and let it be dry. Let it be as thick and as long as your thumb; squeeze out the juice into oil, then hold it over the fire, and apply the cautery between the forcele and the neck, and two small ones slightly descending in the part beneath the chin; and two between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclined a little backward; and one at the heel, and another above the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on either side of the heel below the cautery between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but apply it openly as if smelling it.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And it was said by some ancient that no man uses the fire cautery in imitation of rasur, and heats it and places it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess; and then the pain is gone, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or fistula comes which cannot be cured.
de la mice	from the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not improve, then apply three methods of cautery that are all good.
