Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one method is that you make three or four cauteries, aligning according to the length of the mouse, as per the shape of the liver cautery we have said before; and do not press your hand on all parts of the cautery, and let the patient often lie on his back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two prongs, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is near the mouse, or where the pain in the patient comes from the left side, and let the elevations you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After letting the two inflamed nerves burn until the cores are pierced from the other side, then remove the cautery, and thus it will be four. And if you see, burn all the cautery to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has gotten putrefaction over time, and it is good to change to another of the treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	for dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery is not suitable for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment is not effective, then you must make four cauterizations around the mouth, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one at the anus. Let the cauterizations be close to the skin of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After let the cautery open to drain pus long enough, and do not leave the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and the two intentions would be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly should be kidney-shaped as shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is mentioned above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in a dropsical person and are full of yellow bile, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the thumb and the index finger; and remove your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, otherwise it would burn to a fine ash, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make on two legs two cauteries in each leg at the point of the cuticular; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other above, in between the leg; and leave the cauteries long without curing, as the ash will come out; after that cure the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	of the resetting
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution from the belly comes from cold and moisture, as the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened and cannot be cured by ordinary means; and you see the patient suffering greatly with strong vitality, then make the large cautery on the stomach according to what he has spoken of earlier about the stomach cautery, at which the circulatory cautery is used; and four cauteries between the cheekbones underneath each large cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make the fire cautery on the knife, and one cautery on each hip, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	for the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are external or internal, and are old, being large cold and moist humors corrupted, if the cure has not been effective as we said in the divisions, then make cauteries: III on the spine of the back, that one slightly above the iliac crest, gradually making a triangular pattern, and one cautery below the navel II dobs; and if you think his stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and there is swelling of the skin, then make the large cautery on the stomach as previously mentioned, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen for the entire length of the cautery; let the cautery remain open long.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, let the limb heal until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carbuncle which is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you treat the carbuncle, heat the cautery to resemble a razor, and then place it entirely burning on the carbuncle. Let your hand remain there until the vein begins to appear, from which the blood will flow; do this once or twice. If there is much carbuncle, cauterize each part as we have said. Afterward, apply beneficial ointments until it heals. If you cauterize with a large cautery on a carbuncle, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure a cut or incision, which we shall discuss in its place, comes such an illness that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is any fistula and is enveniled and filled with rotten moisture, you must probe it entirely with a sharp探针，并确保它穿过整个瘘管。并且你要知道整个探针的长度。
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery to a scorching heat, and inserting it into the fistula according to how deep the probe entered, repeat the application of the cautery until the rotten and corrupted flesh is burned, one or two or three times as needed; and be careful not to burn the nerves or large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, beware of these sores, and do not make them worse except in living flesh, and think that it is not personable; after curing the sore until it is healed, and if the flesh is scarred and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the sore is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the flesh is tough, and the bones at the root are corrupted; and in such cases as one we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys and is accompanied by great wind, and does not take on a female form, then you must make a cautery on both sides of the kidneys with the clavile cautery as we have already said; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will do greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a fire cautery in the part below on the bladder, where the hairs begin near the knife's edge, both on the right and left. Let each cautery be as long as one inch of our finger; and make a cautery above the spine, or there if you need it. Make the cauteries sharp according to the form previously stated.
de la marris	of the gallbladder
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the gallbladder is cold and moist, and does not allow conception as a result, and the stones are corrupt and their passage is delayed; and when they come, great pain is felt: then it is necessary to make three cauteries between the buttocks, as we have said for the bladder, and two cauteries above the spine; and make the cauteries sharp, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the socket of the hip, and for this reason it dislocates from its place, the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the cause is found in the departure of the joint space. Then you must cauterize the patient on the socket of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the joint around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have such a cautery, make three cauteries with olive oil, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all the joints. Cure him until he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the socket of the hip, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is treated as we said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the large humors with foul pills or other good pills similar.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterwards, you apply the cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, with medicines that are hot together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many methods, of which one is as follows: you cauterize on the socket of the hip with three triangular cauteries in this form, and make them good in depth and large, with an inch of space between each cautery. Let the cauteries be olive-shaped; once done, a single cautery is made in the middle at the head of the hip, so there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a manner that the circles contain all the hip, and all the parts of the thigh be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way we treat sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not extend to the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then apply two cauteries where the patient says the pain is felt, and above the ankle four inches, a little on the left side; whether the cautery be cutaneous or burn the thickness of the thigh. And if the patient feels the pain extends to two inches or three of the foot or near it, then cauterize where he feels the pain three or four points with the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is greater, do more of this; and if he feels that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then apply the cautery with a surgical or circular instrument, and be well careful in all your cauteries that you leave no part of the cautery unburned so as to burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not do greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who applied the cautery to the ankle of the foot and left it on so long that the leg became entirely swollen, and the foot as well, and all the feet were perforated and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a belly purge from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, apply the cautery to both, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sage said about the cautery of the hip, of which here is the manner, make such iron and let it be at the head as thick as one nailhead of the thumb, or a bit less, and let it be interwoven and let it be between the interweaves from one interweave just to the other distance the quantity of a knot of an inch; and let the interweaves above two parts, and let them also like peas, and may have the hand of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is completely red and gives off scents, and then place it on the socket of the sick hip, and turn it toward the healthy side; and with the cautery once the heat has been applied, leave it for three days; and then make a plaster with butter, and keep the wound open long enough; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this fire cautery little due to fear of its heat, and we see few who use it; nevertheless, he is a good cautery for those who can bear it, and let it be placed where it adheres.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The fire cautery in medicine is such that you make the instrument of tongs in which hangs the margin of the tip, and may be made of tin or iron on a long wall, and at its height it has two palms, and each has the quantity of the thickness of one thumb; and they should be open front and back, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the hip box on the patient lying on their side, place your hand firmly over the hip box; then throw in between the two circles of the hot aw that has been heated by fire just a little, and let it remain for about an hour to several hours, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burning from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is found to be similar to a bite from a snake; and when the bite has passed, withdraw your hand with the instrument and raise the hip gently, and leave thus for three days, and apply butter until the blackness from the cauterization is removed; and let it be three days until putrefaction is treated; and this would be the last aid after the treatment of ointments until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, perform the operation gently according to what you have done for the hip increasing it; and this is the manner of the warm application, and I have written about treating the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If it has a small hole that a point of a razor could enter; and place over this one another pot well leaded, and put ashes and chalk and soft awn on top, until there are two of these above the powders you will have thoroughly prepared by hand; and let it be thus until the liquid descends with water and wax or can be leaded, then take all that awn and throw it over the chalk and over the alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very watery and is administered in doses of medical work and in cauteries of other members. For it does as much work as fire, and to other medicines with which one cauterizes well the haunch, as with terebinth and honey, anacardium, chalk with soap; all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure for someone who was cured of hip pain and sciatic vein pain, and the good man, and he says that no other treatment was done, and that he was healed in one time when this cure was performed, and he bathed as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says that you should take fresh and dry verdigris, grind it a great deal with a little fat, and apply it to the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is located, and leave it on for three hours and by the quantity so that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter the bath until his body is a bit warmed up, and put him to bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such a fire cautery with these medicines if it is not after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with sheeps' wool, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and grease it with old oil, and apply it to the depression between the big toe and the other toe called the fossicle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards, take dry sheeps' wool and heat it on fire until it becomes coals, and place it on the wool, and let it remain until it is extinguished; and do this again, and continue in this manner until you think by sense that it has reached the hip, and the pain has ceased; and this way of cauterization is called "sheeps' wool cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain from the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back through falling or percussion or through excessive bloodletting or through similar spread of cold matter, none of these conditions warrant cautery, though it may be necessary for those caused by the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After this, if the patient is void of fetid pills or other similar conditions, make three lines signed with enche on the back where the pain resides, and in each line use five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make three or four cauteries at the medium clavicle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes upon small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a tight throat when they rise, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and find it cured, cauterize it with the circular fire cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So cauterize each part of the spine thoroughly and evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, cauterize between the spines with a sharp fire cautery for two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treat the limb until it is healed according to what we have said, and be sure not to apply a fire cautery in flesh where there is a space near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain from the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain from the joints is due to moisture spread throughout each limb of the body, and when pain comes from the feet, which the physicians call "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by treatments or medicines, it is treated with cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick the face of the foot, let the cautery be at the entire cautery where we claim "point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come down to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, let the cautery be applied to each knee three or four times from each part, with the entire cautery being olive oil; and if you have need of more, then do more, but keep your hand away only as much as the coals of the fire are hot.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, then apply the cautery that we have said in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make pricks along the flax two lines; and if there remains any pain in the fingers, make pricks on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and gentle medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge the humor, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the side
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in organs, and the bowels descend to the coccyx and it is newly occurring, then it must be that when you see him treated, he should not eat any of that day; and if he uses things that empty his stomach, so that the fumes descend from his stomach; after this, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his buttocks until the bowels are repaired, and draw them with your fingers, and sign under the rupture over the bone of the thigh, and make a mark that be like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and emits scents.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then draw the bowels back to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return. Work well on the thighs of the patient, and set a cushion and a soldier under the thighs, and another under the foot which holds his hands. Then place the cautery over the mark with your whole hand, and keep it straight until you reach the bone. If you do not reach the bone the first time, repeat again until you come to the bone. Be subtle that the bowels do not protrude when you make the cautery; so as not to burn them, and that the patient does not die or other harm occurs.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you cannot reach the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it must be that the cauteries for children are subtle according to the size of their body, and those for adults as large according to their measure; after three days, cure the place of the cautery with butter until the scalding is removed; afterwards, apply other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient rest on his back for forty days until the wound is well sewn up; and it must be that its nursing is prolonged, so that the boils do not burst when he is taken into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, apply a well-made bandage, and let it rest for another forty days; have good rest, letting him work little and guarding against excessive intake of food and drink, and raising his voice too high; and when he follows this instruction, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after the treatment to cut in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not increase further, then let them be seared with the cautery according to their quantity, and let it be burned at one-third of the core; after the treatment according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should sear it with a cautery at three angles in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark the head of the wound with a sign and draw a line along the width above the rupture, and another below it, and guide your cautery through both lines.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, due to falling or injury, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins," and the cauterizations should be according to the length of the limb and its size and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the first cauterization is effective, that is well; but if not, you must repeat the other cauterization over it, for it is customary that the pain should move to the nearest part of the limb, so you must make the cauterizations until the patient is cured.
de meselerie	of leeches
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Leeches are sometimes aided by cauterization with great help, especially for diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you can see the cauterization, take care that the disease is in the beginning, and it is cured as we have said in the division, and does not worsen or linger. And if you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make V cauteries on the head: I place one at the top of the head near the crown, and another towards the front at the end of the hairline; II on the two horns (temples), and III behind on the occiput. Let your hand remain until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs fall off so that the vapors from the gross humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse (nape of the neck) according to what is described above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is spread everywhere; and it appears clearly, then you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and the cautery on the nose, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large on the breast and another opposite, and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the last heel, do not burn them; and at no time make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do cautery, the more you do help, and it profits them; and know that the sick do not feel pain at the cautery as the healthy do, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be that the cauteries are large and small according to the members and joints, according to those you will find in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure, apply a dressing of flour with honey and other dressings until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines and oils and poultices, and it is not yet healed, then make cauteries on the member according to the size and smallness of the member; and let the cauteries penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin; then dress with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes the cautery is done by hand and with a stick or on the back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; and in any case, do not perform it if one is not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of calluses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is fully developed, and medical remedies are ineffective, then cauterize with a cautery slightly strong, according to the thickness of the skin, until the blanchor is removed, and its color changes; then cure with flour of wheat and lentils mixed with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood from colt and almond, one part of each; mix them all together, and apply with a cloth, and keep at the site until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cauterization treatment for a chancre
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre begins to appear, and you see it stopping, cauterize with a circular cautery around the entire circumference of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the surgeons said that one should make a cautery also at the middle of the ulcer; and in all cases this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen more than once; and it is a better thing for it to be cauterized between, with the cautery called "circle," as we said when speaking of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati," and it is slow to heal due to its excessiveness or the oldness of the patient (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see that it should be hastened to heal: then cauterize around a lot of small cautery marks by pricking; after which let it remain thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Car she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through the entire cautery, heat the cautery as described here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of the disease called "adubelati" until the cautery pierces the heart, and make the cautery such that the patient feels it from above in such a way that the course of putrefaction is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing but a corruption of the member, for it eats away at the limbs as fire does to dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a patient who can endure cautery with all fire, then heat the fire cauteries very little and much, according to what is suitable for the patient or where the disease is; after cauterizing from all sides until you erradicate all the corruption, and let nothing remain of it, that everything that is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and place sore-wrapping with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the application of ointments producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not arise, that is good; and if it does not, then restart the cauterization on what remains dislocated from the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture has sometimes been cured with aqueous medicine instead of the fire cautery; but nevertheless, the fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the aqueous medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of corns that come from the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that from the feet, through corns, a disease arises called "clous" according to our understanding, and it is a large, hard thing that causes pain in the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, the fire cautery, and the cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the cautery feather as one would a Gothic pen quill, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can hold the nail in all parts, and that there be subtle margins; after this, put it hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the tip of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to fester with putrefaction; then make a plaster of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the plaster all night, and the nails will fall out and be uprooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then anoint the limb with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire on the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, you must apply a hot cautery to it; and it is done in this manner: take a sparrow’s nest or iron rod, or a Gothic pen quill, and place it over the nail and the althelia (which are used for verrucas); then put the rod on so that it penetrates all around, and pour a little hot water onto it, and hold your hand well, pressing with your hand as you turn it so that the margin of the rod comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot water deep path to the roots; and allow the patient to endure a bit the scalding from the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot itself completely from its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you dry all that is in the body, then treat the wounds that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	treat the shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or nerves, or from quartan fever or other fevers, it is fitting that you make four or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one at the head, and one on the stomach with the olive cautery; if this stops the trembling, and hastens the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At times apparent by inspection of the body bathed, or pus-filled blisters, that come from large corrupt matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary at the first sign that a cauterization be done on each head of the pustule: a fine fire cautery from juniper wood, whose points are heated by fire, or from long aromatic root, or with a lentile-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes the cauterization is done at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they do not grow into large tumors, but the superfluous parts that cause them are cut off, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great hemorrhages from the artery that is cut during the wound, or incision of the abscess, or with the cauterization of the member, and similar things; and it is a most grievous thing to stink.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very tightly until the blood is calmed beneath your finger, and no more drips out; then put the olive fire cauteries, both small and large, over the fire until they are all red hot; then take one, whether large or small according to the wound and the limb in which the artery runs, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood is coagulated.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you remove your finger from above the vein, and the cauteries are still hot, so take one of the other cauteries quickly which are over the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is coagulated; and watch that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; know that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be well coagulated by itself when the artery is large, unless it is done through one of the four methods we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong tying with thread, or by medicines applied which have the power to coagulate blood; and let it be tied and held firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who administers astringent treatments with tightly wrapped cloths or places burning things there, or other similar things, if it does not help much, then do not proceed.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no sight or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and extend it well so that it is constricted above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but rub the palm with cold water frequently until it is very cold, so that the blood is frozen and thickened and constricted; and then proceed to cauterize and medicate as needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter where fire cautery or cautery from burning medicine is necessary for all diseases, and the ointments and their causes and instruments and forms of cauterization; and I have placed that chapter from head to feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way because one finds more easily what one wishes.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And since I begin this one, you must, dear friend, know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first on fire cautery, and because of this, it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many people come for treatments in various ways.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come in such a state that their illness has weakened them so much that they die lightly from the severity of their disease, and from the greatness of their wickedness; one must have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these, there are those who give you their sense and say: "Wait, I am cured"; but the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you in this manner. But place more careful consideration in your honor than in your greed, and do not offer rashly but wisely of what you are certain and have tested. And use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health; and this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May our Lord give you good understanding and justice, and if you wish to receive the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter by discussing it section by section, as in the chapter on fire cautery, which I previously discussed from the head down to the feet, because you find it easier to understand what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head filled with fluid
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes very often to children at birth, and when the bails hold too tightly the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from the reason given that no one knows.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and among all those I have seen, death hastened; for this reason, it seems to me that it would be best to abandon the work in partial treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen the child whose shoulder was full of fluid, and the head grew larger each day to the point it could no longer bear it; and so much moisture gathered beneath the bone at the syphac, between the skull and the bone; and the operations must be such that if there is moisture between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a wide slit in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, as far as the moisture extends; and see here the form of the syphac.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is greater, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are the corners of the face open on each side, and a hard lump jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not respond: then you must make three cuts in the forehead according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture outwards.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After binding the cuts with cloth and powder, and applying wine and oil, leave it thus for five days; then remove the bindings, treat the wound with dressings and ointments, and allow the forehead to heal evenly. Then give the patient dry meat with a little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look for the center of the abscess and the collection of pus; for it is sometimes in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Mark then where the abscess is centered, and the filling of the pus, and make the cut according to what you can do; and beware that you do not cut an artery; and watch for a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the discharge of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When a person has a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or the testicle, and the disease is ancient, and medical treatment does not help, then the last remedy is the cautery with those where they will cauterize the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see the veins pop out, the patient should turn their head; after which, rub the neck with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, then squeeze the patient's neck around the entire cloth; then observe where the vein lies, and the joints of both sides are behind the ears, and slightly raised; then mark the joints with a pen, then cut each one from an acute spatula blade in two parts, so that the cut reaches the bone, and this should be done by the side of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, place the spatula blade over the artery and cut above it, cutting as twice through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will flow out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to touch, you must measure the length of a thumb's breadth three times, then prick with an awl and cut just to the bone; the amount of blood that should be let out is six cents, and by chance perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains on the bone point of syphilis, apply the salve we used for abscesses, and let it not fester, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	From the vein.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old vein disease comes, and acute cataract, due to the moisture of tears and the heat in the temples and ancient scarred fever and similar things, and these are treated with methods of medicinal treatments, yet none of this benefits them, then extract the arteries in the temples and apply cauterizations, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them so is that the patient makes behind the hairs of his temples, and hears the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is little responsive outside except in some very cold persons; and if it is responsive, the patient draws his neck with some strings, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and wipes the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatillum of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then brand the skin lightly until you see the artery, then draw it upward with the forceps, and remove well the threads beneath each part; and if the artery is delicate, turn it with the point of the needle, then cut from that part according to the quantity of two shoulders.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will never heal completely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw off blood from the VIth vein, just to the IIIrd; and if the artery is large, you must tie it with two loops of a double strong silk thread, so that putrefaction does not occur before the sudden opening of the wound, and hemorrhage; then cut the excess between the two ties in that same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the cutellaire cautery to the bone as long as the shoulder is cut; and this is the major work, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries are helpful to finish the moistures; for they are of greater help to the moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the arm with old cotton and place a well-made bandage over it; when you release them, they should be treated with dry medicines that produce flesh and bandages until they are healed; and if there is no cloth from the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten by cauterization, or fill the arm with vitriol cloth and squeeze it with your hand so that the blood congeals; and if you do not have this present, place your thumb over the cloth until the blood congeals, and rinse the cloth with cold water until the blood stops, and hold it as needed; what is more moist and lighter in the extraction of the artery should be cauterized at the vein from this cutting cautery divided into two parts, but the cuts should be well thick to ward off their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too cold, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a piece of ginger between the two knives, and then when you have signed the edges of the two lips, and you place the hot iron until it comes just to the bone, cut the vein in two lips; and keep them apart between the two heads because they are not entirely sealed by this cautery from start to finish; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes flow down the veins that are above the test of the head, and applying any medical treatment does not help, you see the face of the patient become flushed, and feel or observe tremors on the forehead; and the eyes are cold and moist to such an extent that even paper hair falls out, and the papers become heated and scorched by the warmth of the tears, so it must have this treatment.
