Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "bruise cure," and you should do this for a patient who has this illness: if he has hair on his forehead, make three equal incisions along the length of the forehead; let one incision be as deep as two nails going down to the bone, and the others two above the muscles on both sides, but beware not to cut the arteries that are on both sides above the muscles; keep your hand away from the continuation of the lower jawbones, and each wound should be about the size of three nails crossing over; have a piece of sponge and much linen ready for wiping the blood, then apply the sharp spatumile from either side as shown.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is from the temple to the second incision; and scorch all the flesh which is above the bone between the two cuts. Then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove the spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert into the first incision the instrument called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is rough, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the scalpel cutting edge towards the buttock side of the wound, and the rough edge towards the bone, and continue inserting it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And scoop out all the vessels that descend to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to what opens at the buttock side, and then do the same in the middle incision down to the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, press out the wound for the blood taken; then place a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put wet cloths in wine and oil and vinegar, and guard that abscesses do not form; and on the third day remove the bandages, and apply a large dressing with warm water, then cure with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other wound treatments until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of eye pain
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone frequently comes down with a severe catarrh, and you see the eyes turned inward and small, and a weakening of vision, and burned papers; and the hair falls out, and there is a pain akin to water in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that these materials and this catarrh come from many veins, and the place where they are, it is here.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to lie on their back behind their forehead, then make a large incision between the forehead, and another slightly wider one.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the left temple incision to the right temple incision, and let the incisions go until the bone is exposed; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move with eating. When the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two edges of the incision and place old cotton, and linen; then cover with moistened cloth in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with things that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In a manner thus: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of calamine, and make a plaster from them; and apply it to the wounds to draw out flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or ore or similar things such as iron; or seed, such as wheat, beans, peas; or flowing substances such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear as a stone or some other substance that does not attach to the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it distills any drop of violet oil or silk oil, then administer its extraction; and let the patient expectorate with ease, and plug the nostrils when expectoration comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool in the ear; and hold the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes out in this treatment; and if it does not come out, then administer its extraction with fine forceps, of which the form is described here.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; but if not, administer extraction with a delicate oncine of small size; and if it does not come out with this, make an ear spica and insert the head of the spica or hole in the ear firmly, and plug what is around the spica with soft wax so that the liquid cannot enter with the spica; then draw it out forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take glue, dip the tweezers into it, and put any instrument that is sharp for this purpose. Then place a bit of cotton inside; afterwards press the glue over the stone or whatever it may be, and draw it out forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not burst from all these things that we have said, you must quickly cut the ear as with an abscessed, hot, and painful one; and spasm. The manner of cutting is that you first apply a cautery to the patient's head, and draw out the blood according to its measure of virtue, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; and let the cut be as round as the moon until you reach the stone, then extract it according to your power, and suck it quickly with your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is enclosed and swollen, administer the extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the small spatule according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tongs and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the earwax that falls into the ear, the patient should use nose blowing to clear the first conditions, and clean the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the wax is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it falls out forcefully through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If this is not the case, take many stones according to the length of your strong tendons, and warm them slightly in fire; then put one or several of the patient's earwax into the wound, and cut on the outside of his foot from another side, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this from stone to stone until the pus is all gone, and then she will be all gone; and if you see, take a rush, and put one of the heads into the ear, and the other head near fire until the softer rush is burned; then do it with other rushes as we said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, as a flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size and can be felt, administer the extraction with forceps; and this is the thing easiest to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you examine the ear in the sunlight: if there are no apparent worms, you draw them out with fine forceps, and if they do not appear, you take the wire of which this is formed.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow inside and wide outside.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finest needle into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient feels, then gradually push the wire completely through; do this often until all the worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, plug the inside of the wire with cotton as I have said for the stone; and if they do not emerge forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the incision of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and you should distill your eyes and medicines into the ear through this instrument, as shown by its form.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or lead thin over the small ports, and above the outlet to distil; and for pressing within the distillation use a well-made tool of lead for this purpose, and if you choose to use a razor and envelop the tip with suitable cotton; then throw your eye or your juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the cannel, and let the cannel be in the ear; then pour inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or movement from the ear; and let the medicine sense the malady within, and let the distillations be a little heated on the fire as one distils into the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicines would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who has no perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to men due to a wound stopping up, or flesh growing inside the ear, and these stoppages come sometimes completely blocked in the ear, so one cannot see them; and sometimes just a small part of the perforation closes, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes completely blocked, so one cannot see it, is of great concern for proper treatment, and in such cases where you can see, you must place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, then the work has almost completed as described.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be hot and cutting both in front and behind entirely clean, so that it does not blister the ear; if the purgation is of living flesh or a part of the ear, hold it with fine forceps, and remove it gently, until all that flesh is completely taken out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the purgation is performed in the ear, take the fine scissors lightly and heat them a little with fire, then place them on the part of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense the purgation from which the patient feels pain in the ear, prick it gently, and make sure you do not damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a wick according to the width of the puncture, and soak it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day while the wound is healing, or take a tent and fat in rose-colored water, and powder over ground vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, it must be treated with the tent and move another moistened tent made from rose oil and wax until the swelling is gone; then treat until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bloodletting comes, plunge a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments which remove the flow of blood that are or treat by distillation.
de la char des papieres	from the juice of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that comes from papers of eyes when they are moist and are dry, it must be that you extend them with tongs and forceps, and the decoction of a spoonful of its roots; then put on the head ground vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decortic peace, one cauterizes with the subtle lentile cautery, and the cauterer after incision moves; many times they return, since no thing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times in the eyes come things like gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "hail," and it is an assembly of moisture large on the paper above and below; the work is such: observe if the hail moves from one part to another, and that is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then burn each part lightly, then take it with tongs, and apply it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot change it without piercing a little the paper, it does not grieve the patient; and if the tear is large, sew it up with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force much, for the ointments restore it quickly and promote flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the stone is descending into the inner ear toward the upper part, pour out the paper, and place the stone with tongs, and turn it from one side to another; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not grieve the patient; and when the stone is removed, wash the eye with salt water, and cure the area until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is embedded in the membranes of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and greatly affects their eyes. They often have catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; for this reason, they lie on their faces, sleeping with them down, and are covered by their damp papers that swell and hide from the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the head between your hands and feel the exinach within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is as follows: the patient places their head on your lap; then take a linen cloth, and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach that each part contains. Then place it over them; press with both hands from one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered within the circle. Then make a slit through the moist area, cutting a crack wide enough, but not larger than the incision made in the healthy vein; and scrape the skin thoroughly until you see the exinach. And through many such preparations, exinach comes out from the slit, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the wound with one piece of linen cloth between your hands; turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is separated; take care not to widen the incision, so that you do not reach all the way to the socket near the eye, and do not damage it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the extraction does not open at the beginning of the incision, widen the incision slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then apply moist cloths and water, and place on the wound, and extract with gauze.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who grind grain and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an hot abscess comes to its head, apply the cure of plasters soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on papers hairs grow other than their nature, and they are matured, they harm the eyes, and bring about conditions like habitual tearing, softening of the papers, and albugine, to such an extent that it is a cause of eye destruction; and the cure according to four methods: either by fire cautery together with heat, or by aqueous medicine as described in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by cains, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the eye of the patient in your healthy hand, then turn the paper from the oil side to your left hand; if it changes color, that is good; if not, put a needle along the entire length of the thread above; and let this be between the margin of the paper or where the additional hairs grow among these hairs, and draw the thread across the paper, then cut it flatly. Then make a slit in the part beneath the paper, beneath the added hairs, to the spatumile completely, from the large tearer until the small one; then remove the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and flannel under the paper, then apply a figure of enche above the paper, like the leaf of myrtle, and always ensure that the figure is according to the quantity you wish to lift from the paper which is divided for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs much of the paper according to how the paper has been softened; then make on all the surface between the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large lacrimal gland until small; let it be one of the cracks near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then pour an ounce at one of the two corners of the cheek, then scorch all of it; then join the two lips with a stitch using a fine needle throughout the entire thread of thin wool, and wipe away the blood, and do away with the excess threads on both sides of the sorcery to any gluey things, if you wish to do this; and if not, do not care about it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitches using drying and constraining things, because the paper revives suddenly from the wound and their joining, but the stitching is worn (as the ancients say), and these are works without fear; and in another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as like the leaf of laurel, as we have recounted, sized at three inches according to the form which is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply those which surpass the small forces equally according to the form which is given here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, take a needle or have thread, and put one end of the thread through the figure; and place the other thread next to the large artery, and the second thread next to the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads equally; then remove your hand equally, and remove all the skin above which you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suturing, and treat until it is healed; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar healing ointment; and any time the hair of the paper is reversed: you must use what we said about the incision; but the suturing in both places is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of cankers is as follows: and it is that you fold the paper and cut an opening inside according to what I have said, and then make two canker rods by art, and two thin threads also long as the paper and the width of the space between your fingers; and hold the heads of the two parts where you will hold the strings; then join one and the other subtly above that which rises from the eye of the paper, and pull the two cankers from both sides; and let it be so for some days, and the skin which was constrained shall die and nerve and fall off, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays healing, and if it grows strong, then continue the treatment until it is healed; and when the wound has healed, and the paper is lifted, and no hair will grow anymore; and this is the form of the two cankers that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you insert a thin needle, and you thread the fine silk thread through it; then assemble the heads and tie them together carefully, so that the lengths of the threads make up one palm's length; then arrange another fine silk thread in the chase, and tie its head to the other thread; then place the patient's head on your healthy side; and keep away from the sun so that the operations become clear, for it is a subtle and small operation. Then insert the needle completely into the root of the added hair, and make it pierce through the banner paper quickly as you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair if there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out through the chase with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not grow with it, you shall draw the chase out through all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase seems to be fully drawn out from above and that you see it by the sight of the eye; then you shall draw the chase and the thread, and close the wound for two or three days, until the hairs soften in their place and flesh grows over; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of natural hair, and let it be removed with that or where you leave it, until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the putrefaction of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or putrefaction, comes to the oil, it does so in two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or a cut, or a fire cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut the sutures, and分开其边缘，然后放入亚麻布绷带，并且等到它愈合后再移除；在治疗中不应使用干燥和收缩性的东西。
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And if you do this, the disease returns worse than the first; but use substances that soften, such as fenugreek; and wash with water or urine and boiled linseed, and ointments of clarified butter in any of the eyes, and wrap it in a cloth, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal entirely according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are only for addressing the disease so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds, splits, cauteries, and similar things; and the way of the work is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and fix it into the flesh, and make the thread pierce from left to right so that the threads come out at both heads of the flesh; then place the flesh above all on the needle, and the cloth over the spatumile wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the crack, turn the paper, and make two cracks inside the paper; and let the heads of the two cracks be at the angles of your incision, and make an angle such that when they are assembled, the figure is also like the figure of a letter which has no "I griesche"; then remove the flesh according to the quantity that its sides have over, from what follows the paper, then join the separated parts with a thread of wool; then apply the cure as we said for mollifying medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a crack or stitch or cautery, you must make a full crack below the hairs of the paper, and according to what is said before; then separate between the two flaps of a tent as I have said; and one should perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is much diverse in form. The master surgeons devise any means possible so that they can make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what needs to be done and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sewing occurs in the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is hardened with the white of an egg and cannot move or perform its natural work, then it must be that you insert the point of a needle beneath the paper and pull it up; and stretch it with forceps until you cut what is aerated at the subtil spatumile, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting so that the patient cannot bear that the spatumile too sharp bleaches the eye; and make your incision, which you burn together, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all this assembly is healed, and never causes ailing in an aqueous saline substance, or from anger; then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye moistened wool soaked in plenty of egg; and after three days use binding and other soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail of the eye is according to two manners: it is nervous and similar to a hard membrane, and another which is not nervous but is similar to white congealed moisture, such that when one touches it with iron and tends it properly with scissors, one cannot see; and both resemble starting near the large lacrimal gland, and grow little by little until they cover all vision and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your hand, then closes their eyes. You lift the paper with your hand, then clip the nail with small-pointed scissors and hold it above. Then take a needle, and insert the horsehair, or oxhair, or beef hair, and a strong thread; and slightly double the point of the needle and push it through the nail, piercing it completely with the entire needle. Hold the nail with the thread and position it above, and scrape along the side of the nail where the groove and silk meet to the tip of the hair up to the head. Then cut away the remainder at the root of the lacrimal gland with all subtle force, leaving the natural skin or lacrimal gland, so that the incision does not cause the body to weep accustomed tears; and sometimes you hold the nail only on a pinch and on the thread as we have said; then scrape it along the entire subtil spatumile (a small canal) where its form is.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatule does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the probe is not perforated; and after incision pour in the eye a little sieved salt, and from the collar made of litharge, and let it be until the next day; then cure with that which he needs until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot pierce it with the needle, and the forceps cannot enter it, often this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it copulate, work on the eye of the patient, and take the spatule light and slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And scrape the nail gently from above, and if you see that it thins at all and the rationale presses on it, distill from your mouth into the eye a collar of litharge and a red collar and sieved salt, and stop up the eye until the next day; then restart the other work according to this same operation until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against it in the eye, such as an abscess, then let it be, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the gland causes great harm to the eye, suspend it by an oncine, and remove a part but not all, so that no tears arise; then distill in the eye red powder made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh that arises around the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men's eyes grow red flesh once, and cover the pupil, restrain it on papers and turn it upside down, seeming like a water lily; and the work is that the patient places their head on your side, then manipulate the eyes, and remove all that flesh with suitable oncines, and suspend it by force; then scrape off the first layer of flesh, continuing to shave until you reach the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the work. For the incision of the spatumile as we have said in the incision of the nail and with small forces one removes the sebel, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all flesh is removed, apply brine oil or distill red powder and similar corrosive medicines, and place a swab upside down over the eye. If nothing remains and the wound heals without an abscess, if you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that calm a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and in this way remove any new flesh that appears in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But still it must be that you adjust the treatment of each weak eye from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If the veins around the eyes are red and cover the eye, and affect vision and weaken the eye for all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the first thing you must do is to examine whether the eye itself is red and clear, and there is no other disease besides the redness; then handle it in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy hand, and suspend those veins for one inch according to your wisdom, and let the inches be doubled carefully according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be one ounce by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil the veins subtly and wipe the blood an hour after another, until you see remove those veins from the eye; and guard that you do not scar the eye with the points of the forceps, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be most fervent in your work so that you do not harm any vein; and when you have done this, distill in the eye a cologne of green and red to corrupt what is left of the swelling.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to coil all of those in that hour, apply a poultice to the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and assured of the warm abscess, then resume according to this method which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the veins.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire [fistula] is called "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and with hot aqueous medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then indeed in it you make a cut above the abscess, let it die where it should, and draw out all the moisture that it has, until the bone is revealed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is revealed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then remove it with all the instrument of which this is the form; and it is called "asper chief," and it should be made from iron to the head round, and should be pointed like a rasp as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the head of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little so that you know that this corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the head of medicinal drying substances.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is sewed, and flesh arises, and the core of the bone is sewed, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not renew or is not abscessed, and bad accidents do not occur, know that it is healed; if this is not so, there is no other means than to bring the fistula to the hole of the vein according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with wet medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the awl according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the handle be attenuated just to the tip as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the socket of the shoulder, and keep your hand away from the eye for a little while, then turn to all the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the pain if he keeps his hand near his nose; and then restore the joint with medicines dry as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the joints, the matter goes to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are completely open, and there is no further discharge or reduction, it is necessary to bind the patient. Then, treat the wound, and place cups or hasterels over the eye without piercing for suction. Afterward, apply a paste of myrrh and aloes and incense and sarcocol at the site. Then, keep the eye bound with bandages and cloths; the method for the cloths is to use sufficiently soft cloths, double each one four times, and place them one on top of another according to the amount needed. Then, cover from above with a hard form cloth, and reapply cups for suction without piercing. Remove the cups and allow the eye to be bound day and night; if the ligature becomes soft, you must apply it much tighter. After removing the ligature at day and night, if you see the eye healing, it is good. If not, continue applying the paste, cloths, ligatures, and cups until fully healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the tearing of woollen cloth or skin
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woollen cloth or skin, then opened, and come forth like the grain of resin, and is shocking to see; when you see it copered, the works are such that you pierce a needle into the root of the part beneath until above, then pierce another needle where there be double thread from the part of the suture. And make the piercing, and let the first needle according to its disposition; then cut the leu of the double thread and tie a part of the eye around it, and hold it tightly, then remove the needle and put on the eye a cloth moistened in abundance of egg; and let it be until the threads break with the eye, then treat the eye with things that comfort as long as the wound is healed; and at no time restrain the wound from every part of a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes have a great appearance, pierce them with a sharp needle that comes from the inner part of the eye, and drain the moisture and descend the eyes, and let them enter soon; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not due to water that assembles in the eye, seeming like descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you cause the patient to sit on a seat prepared and straight, then take the head between your hands from one side, and move the eyelid until you see the bow come above your eyes; then it should be pierced, and does not descend and removes the light, and see the patient the things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descents of the bow do not appear as we have said, it is.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	if you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and cut on the corneal membrane gently along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the crown, as much as the bow comes out; and when it has come out, distill into the eye with warm water mixed with honey, or boiled fenugreek water and honey, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the appearances of the eye's waters in the division, and what needs to be pierced; work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It must be that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the sunlight, and fix the healthy eye very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if they are right-handed; then take with your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda," or with your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then place the tip of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a hair in that part of the black part of the eye where the minor lacrimal duct is, and push the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand so that it pierces through the black part of the eye, feeling that almagda reaches the empty place; and the measure of the way almagda should be is exactly in proportion to the space from the prunelle to the end of the noirour; and this is the crown of the eye; you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then put the instrument where the water is, and express it through another way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the liquid flows now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a short time, and if the liquid rises again by the second vein, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place and no longer rises, extract it gently by turning your hand little by little; then put a bit of silk thread around it, and remove this from his eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put cotton or moistened wool in oil and abundant egg, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, place on it a compress with abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it hardens to the extent that it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are people whose eyes are too hard, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which the form is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it fine, then pour in the hardened substance as we have said; and for the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a sleeping position in the dark; and let him be free from all movements, and give light meals, and move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and bind him according to his disposition until three days; then release him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and have him show some things, and then rebind him until seven days; and it is not fitting that you do this during or after incision now, but you must loosen it, because the liquid rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses arise, you release the eye before the seventh day, and follow the treatment for one who alleviates an abscess; and when it is pacified, you release the vision and place upon its edge a small cover to protect any day, and let it be attached in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then let it out of the house little by little, and let it heal in its own way; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came to us who were from the Vercelli region, who told us that in their country they made almagda punctum, to which one applied water, but truly I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of almagda, because he who does not know them will see them; and they be properly of arsenic.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of aus be of this same subtlety, and the last in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the cheek below the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes cheeks below the nose appear swollen, of which some resemble scorpions with claw marks; and there are those where the cheek has a deep-colored mark from a bite, and where the cheek has a well-colored sore.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those sores that are not deep, it is necessary to place the patient between your hands facing the sun; work on his nostrils, and sprinkle an ounce on those sores, and draw them out. Then cover what you can bear with a very fine sharp spatumile from one side, until you know that the sore is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be coped, open it with all subtlety and lightly with the instruments, so that nothing remains; and if without surmounts or malignant abscesses occur, give him such help as is proper; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the pus is exhausted and all the flesh be removed, then throw out oil easy and aigle or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the oil works and moisture comes to the palate, know that it is cured; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach for cutting: then you must put a slightly thick thread of linen, and knot it by hand well, with each knot about an inch or less apart; and place the patient's head where the thread comes out into his nose as far as possible, and draw out odorant until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times do so for children at school, and this is a light matter for him who knows how to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them alternately ensuring they are as we say.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it so that you know the nerve has rotted that tissue, then pull the thread, wipe the blood, soften the thread in Egyptian salve, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the salves have corroded all that remains of the tissue; and then put a quince stick in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the brain, into which one distils the oils and medicines or honey.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And may it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a quince stick, and lead it there; and if you see, make a closed stick, and let the instruments be full to purge the brain; and have one hand on the brain to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the head over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	many times a disease arises in the head over the nose which is called "telul", and grows and becomes large there; and when it is visible to look at; and because of this you must cut in the beginning, and remove all of it, then put on it the cautery or the burning medicine; and if one delays cutting until it becomes large, one must beware if it is hard, of a fugitive color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron at all for it is an embedded abscess; for when one cuts it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is from pus contact, not of a fugitive color, and you can see that one can cut it all out, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure it with things drying and constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilages in the work, it profits little, for in some men.
