Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you must see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then adjust the two edges with a stitch, and cure it until it heals. And if the edges are dry on both sides, you must cauterize all parts of their core until they heal, then join the two edges with a stitch, bind it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood powder, and powdered incense; and place over the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another healing plaster, and let it remain until it dries by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is that you assemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said in stitching the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	By hand, abscesses in the lips become hard, resembling grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; then it is necessary to turn the lips, incise each side, and remove the contents with forceps, cleaning each part; subsequently apply oil after the vitriol incision, until the blood is thoroughly cleansed; and then apply balsam, and treat the oil with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a sore develops on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you must hold it with tongs and cut at its root, allowing the pus or blood to flow; then place on the head vitriolated powder, or other contracting and drying powders; and if this sore returns after incision, many times occurring, so cut again the second time, and cauterize: it will not return after the cauterization; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are assembled on the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, escorces that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and worms, as much as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must place the patient's head in your hands, and his chin on your knee, and root out the teeth or escorces that appear, until there is nothing left; and thus deal with the blackness and greenness, and yellowing and other stains, until they are all removed; and if what is said for the first reason is gone, it is good; if not, begin again from the second day and the third, until you have rooted out everything; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments to be rooted out, according to what the work shows, because the rasers used to root out teeth have other shapes than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth in its pain, you should delay the extraction as much as possible, for it must not be done at all if one can help it; for it is a very precious substance until such time that there is no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to extract, it must be that you are certain of the tooth causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain afflicts the patient, and he thinks it is from a sound tooth, and has the good tooth extracted; and yet, all the while, the pain does not depart because the bad tooth was not removed. For we have already wanted to do this for these gentlemen. And when you are well certain of the tooth causing pain, it must be that you burn around the tooth with a very hot iron to protect the gum from all sides; then shake it with your fingers or with fine tongs at first bit by bit, until it is well loosened, then firmly set the tongs; and place the head of the patient on your knee between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After drawing the tooth without breaking it, if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and put it in each part lightly, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it must be filled with wads of cloth, or the holes are to be closed; and you should gently extract it with forceps so as not to break it during extraction; and you must carefully work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it and leave a part of it, as this can cause the patient greater pain than the initial one due to the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act thus as the ignorant physicians do, who by their haste and rashness break sometimes the marrow, and do not bring to it what we have recounted; but they cause to come again certain diseases through the roots that remain, or through the marrow that they break, as we often will; and when the bone is drawn out, wash the wound with wine or ale and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply the wound with vitriol powder; and if this does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments to which one must apply when pulling teeth should be long-pointed and have thick handles, so that they do not double when you are extracting the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large limbs such that they do not bend in the stretching, and made of iron well forged, and with teeth to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during stretching, you must place wet cotton soaked in butter on the shoulder for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the shoulder is softened, then remove the clamps called "algefri," from which the head appears like a bird's beak; and let them be made internally as a file, and that is their form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out through all these clamps, you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is a palanche, and that is its form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be firm and thick so that it does not break, and if it does break at this point, that is good; otherwise, aid with all the instruments, which forms are mentioned later.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if aid is needed from this instrument that has two handles, which is the form of it:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front by reason of the teeth, and from this instrument which seems like large forceps, of which is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be firm so that they do not break. Know that there are many instruments for the teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted. And the master surgeons, through their subtlety, find their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease show them. For there are such diseases where the old ones did not teach any instruments because of the diversity of bones. If they break at all during the operation or other bones, then one searches for the appropriate instruments, as I have said, and aids with gestures, which is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-held to hold the bone, so it does not escape but can be held and removed; then restore the head with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, remove it with all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural order, and the shape is ugly, especially in maiden women, you must know whether the tooth was born out of place and cannot be set or filed: then pull it; and if it is decayed with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is described, and which resembles a small beak, and let it be made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And file it little by little in your hand each day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that you can file it, then file it with a small file as described.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the lime with which needles are made; and on the tooth, file a little at a time in your hands gently, so that it does not move until it sharpens; then in the end shave it flat for any filed cutter, and if the tooth becomes too sharp and blunts the tongue, then you must file away its harshness until it is equal, so that it does not blunt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth chatter
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth chatter due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot hold down what they are eating so they defecate, you should treat them with constricting medicines, but this is not effective; so you must restrain them with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and decay, but gold never changes. Choose a thread that is neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to adjust the teeth, take the thread and bend it double between two healthy teeth, then place the heads of the needles between the medium-sized teeth, whether one or more, until you clearly reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the treatment up to the part where you started, and withdraw your hand skillfully and carefully, so that it does not move at all; and secure the thread at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the head of the tooth with forceps and assemble them, and pin them between the healthy teeth, and place them such that they do not irritate the tongue; and then leave them so tight as they can remain, and if it loosens or the threads break, you must tighten them with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for all its duration, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment figure of the two healthy teeth and the two mesial incisors, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one must put it back in its place, frequently as we have said; and one should not intervene with someone who is not skilled and suffering, and once the form of an osseous bovine tooth is made, it is placed in the spot where the tooth is missing, and it is tightened as we have said, and remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	none of these wounds come from the tongue by nature or any other way; they occur either by accident in a stitched wound; and the works are such that you work the mouth of the patient, have his head on your knee, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous ligament broadly until the tongue is dislocated from its place; and if there is hardness or knotting, which is due to sudden injury, you use a lancet and cut broadly that ligament; and guard that the wound not be too perfect, for the artery is beneath; and when done, lift the head with rosewater and alum, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen tent; and let the patient rest each night so that the leeches cannot suck.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding continues, place vitriol powder on the wound; and if the blood stops, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other salves until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of a red, black, or hard color, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is turning white and there is moisture, throw in a pinch, and cut a fine incision with a lancet, and drain from both sides; and if the blood stops during your work, place vitriol powder until it is healed, then return to your work until you have done everything; then remove the flax and salt, and treat with other salves until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are swellings in the throat called "godath," and these are properly known as the two almonds. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are hard abscesses of small size and flesh-colored, be careful not to touch them with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron at all, nor for the discharge of blood; but leave them until they are ripe, and then you may cut them out, or they would break open on their own. And if they are white in color and the root is fine, have your instrument ready to extract them, but first make sure that the abscess is warm, settled, and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then cause the patient to sit in front of the sun, and his head be in your care, and let him open his mouth and have the sergeant's hand between his hands, and press the tongue under all the instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or of thin tin as of a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take an ounce and stick it in the almond, and draw force above more than you can; and draw nothing from the threads with it, then cover the instrument, of which this is the form, that resembles strong forces; and whatever the heads are curved, one next to the other, and are very sharp, and made of iron ind or of antinne.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use tongs, of which the form is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and on the other side named; and when you have incised one of the almonds, incise the other in the same manner. After the incision, gargle the patient with hot, clear water, or with warm and easy-to-swallow water, and if there is a discharge of blood, gargle the patient with water, or cooked pomegranate peel, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the blood has stopped flowing; then cure the wound when it is healed. And if other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, incise them in the same manner as the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had developed in her throat, that is to say the small abscess; and almost entirely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the conduit being blocked, and neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had to be incised through both openings of the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then quickly, and incised the oncine in one opening, then pulled out a large portion of the bowels; then made another cut in the other neck opening, and cleared her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I incised the abscess again, and filled it with coagulated blood, and only a little blood came out; thus, the passage in the throat was destupeied for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued cutting at this abscess for a long time; the abscess kept reoccurring and filling the space that I had cleared until it became very large; then I bandaged it and cauterized inside the throat: thus, it did not grow any further; and left those matters, and let God decide what would happen to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the swelling is felt in the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and when it is large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are calmed, and it is fine-grained, then it is appropriate to lance it; and that which is round gathered and not long; and which is bloody or of linen color or black, then it is appropriate to avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It must therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument about which we made remembrance before; then put the inch into the eye, and pull out underneath, and cut with the second of the two instruments that I said in the incision of the almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it must be that you do not cut more than the superfluous which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the almonds, and cure it until it is sane.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, it must be that you use an instrument for the cautery to alleviate the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the fire cautery is very painful.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put their head on your lap, and then press their tongue with the instrument we have mentioned or fire cautery, and cover it with live vinegar, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and fill the cavity of this instrument, as described.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let their head have a hair or what one puts the medicine on, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine above the eye; and the patient lie on their side so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, without descending to the throat and tongue. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it above the eye for half an hour, until you see it heated and the bites of the medicine are pacified. And if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the instrument on the cotton in the tube above, so that the cotton dries above the eye; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry for four or five days. And if you need to restart the application of the medicine cautery, do so, and after the cautery, wipe around the eye with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take reed, yarrow, origanum, rue, chamomile, vervain, and similar herbs, and gather all of them or any of them in one pot, and put them easily, and boil; and the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and amid the pot have the instrument fitted according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And may be of silver or lead, and let one of the heads be inserted in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the pipe, until the eye is numbed; after that often repeat, until the eye dries up, and see that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things happen; nor do this when the hot abscess declines.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell inside the head for the patient, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to weigh down on the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether beneficial.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is cut in the throat with a bone or spiny fish bone, or some other thing; so it must be that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue toward the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and that which does not appear to you and lies in the throat, must cause the patient to vomit as if the meat were cooked in the stomach; by chance this may be expelled by vomiting; or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will be cut, and then you will draw out the force; and if it does not come forth from what we have said, take the plucking instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the forceps be applied to the head so that it may more easily enter the throat, and keep the head lifted high; and see that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it swell or the bone move inside; and the patient should themselves hold the instrument, for if they are able or the thing is sore; then let them push down, or he draws it forcefully all at once, equally with the whole instrument, as far as it goes.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat juice
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No juice of the throat is medicated as I said in the division by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look into the throat of the patient in the sunlight, after you press his tongue with the instrument I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it off with a very small needle, or with fine tongs that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a live cane, insert it into the throat of the patient, then blow or move air from the cane with hot iron, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is affected by fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, pour it into the mouth, and give it to swallow, moving it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the blood feels the water, let it go.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not go as we have said, subfuscige the patient with arsenic sulfide, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the uve; do this many times, for it will fall without difficulty.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are live coals, and let it be covered with a perforated cover in the middle, and into that perforation put the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not go out but goes until the blood; and the blood will fall now, and if it does not fall, you must repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty and dry things, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to be forced out by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood, is such that when one can see it, it resembles bent tongs to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot let go. And behold its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings after in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and incision; and there are two ways of which one is in its very resemblance, and from that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the veins where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the solid flesh, and abscesses of the vein are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for abscesses, we must not pierce them until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are such that it is necessary to pierce them when they are ripe, even though they do not die according to their completion, as those abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, and one lets them be until they are rotted within, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or when the abscess is in the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or when it is in the foundation, one should pierce it even if it is dead; it does not matter that you perforate an abscess crust before complete digestion, provided that the one affecting the foundation does not rot completely and remain extended within, and may become a fistula; and cannot heal in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of perforating the abscess that is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and sharpness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where more dependent on the abscess, and where it appears to move. Let the perforations be as long as the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places straight without folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the living flesh, it is better that you leave the perforation until its digestion is accomplished, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body will be lengthened by the venom of it, and it is full of much filth; and perchance the edges and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if for any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, as the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must provide small punctures for small abscesses, and large punctures for large abscesses, and many fissures according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is necessary to lance the core, and cover; when it has become as dry as a flake, and is softened, you must do so as with buboes: and for those that are split into three angles, and for those that are covered like the leaf of laurel, as with abscesses of scrofula; and for those where you make a circular incision, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, as in superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you puncture them completely; and when the abscess is large, and has collected a great amount of pus, if you puncture it, you must not drain all the pus at once in that hour, but rather drain only part of it; then plug the abscess until the next day, and drain again as needed; do this repeatedly from large to small, until all the pus is drained; similarly, if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman pregnant, or young children, or old infirm people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because the patient shudders several times with the release of pus, and by chance the patient dies, and you are not at fault.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, beware of this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, clean the wound, and observe if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a complete cut, administer tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many pores, then it must be that you insert a tent in each so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you let it heal over, then it must be that you fill it with old cotton or the powder of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the bleeding occurs during your work, administer cold water and ease it with a soft cloth, and place it over the area bleeding repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, and it is controlled and treated, and the powders that I have said to use in this book are applied to their wounds, and if it is or seems to be winter, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, then you must place moist cloths on tents and blankets soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the wounds are fleshy, then you must apply moist cloths on blankets soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then open the abscess, drain it, and treat it as needed until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: since I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the shoulders
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses appear on the head, and their appearances are like little bags, much resembling the seeds of a flax plant.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and similar to tumors, and have moisture like those of a chicken's egg; and there are those that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause contrary effects.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the procedures for the flank are such that you test with any instrument called "entromissoire," from which the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, let it out from above through the long incision.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, burn without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it will repeatedly stick if nothing is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if it is present; if not, use water and salt, and apply to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and this will discharge what has remained overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton application as before on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains overnight; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds on to fat, shape the poultice according to this form, long in length; and apply all your ounces, and burn it from all sides, and put all your effort into drawing out the fat where it lies. And if the artery acts contrary, do as I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for the abscess if it is stony, and for cutting and treating as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting into the stony abscess and the moisture is less burdensome, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in some of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and these were the abscesses that I examined from an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a smooth, rough, and white stone, unable to break; and if any had been made of it, one would have done just as well by making a wound with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or head, those that come to the head of children and the roots of the ears, the opening must always be at the lowest part of the neck, so as to allow the bowels to issue out; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes appears elsewhere or on other parts of the body, they are hot, and are joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own site, like the lump and abscess of the neck, as we have said; and the symptoms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some contain moisture, and others are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	For those in which you see good disposition to the touch, and resemble the color of the body, is motionless from every part and is not sore on the neck nor near the artery nor the conduit, and is not very deep; then you should copes it from above, and scorch each part, and keep the two lips of the wound with needles if needed, as we have said for abscesses of the neck. And draw a little at a time, and be sure that you do not cop the nerve nor the vein, and do not let the pus accumulate or cut too deep, that your hand does not slip, and do not go too far, so that you do not cop what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you open the vein or the artery, and it does not allow further work, put in the wound ground glass, or some powders that staunch blood, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is staunch, return to your work until you complete it; then rest according to your proper indication if there remain any small scrofulous swellings, treat and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofulous swelling, it is not fitting that you open that swelling at its root, but ligate it with a double strong thread, and let it fall away through it without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cure the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound, and stitch them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you cut the root of it, pull out the core, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have excess, puncture them where they open naturally; and puncture them as was said before, in dependence, then apply wicks with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, let the ointment cure until it is sane.
de squinance	of scabies
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of the operation of the throat; but I have never seen anyone perform it in our land, and this is their written account.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have scabies, it is necessary to perform the incision of the throat which is called "epiglote"; and no help should be given by this method, because all the veins and the pyron in the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the ampyllae.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pyron, it is necessary to perform the epiglote to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It must therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglote, be cut over three or four small incisions across, between the two circles or by the size of the incision as seen, not in the cartilage; and those who are thus are suitable for the cutting of the epiglote so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it must be stretched from the whole inch of the throat to the chain; and cut through the skin until it comes to the chain; avoid the vessels of blood if you see any, and then cut the syface as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the chain which leaps forth because the vein is ruptured, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which strangulation is suspected, bring together the two edges of the wound in the heart, and suture it soundly over the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim states that this should not be done until the throat is completely paralyzed, and the patient is judged to be dying, then proceed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and for this, the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease passes, and it passes in three or four days. Then they commanded to suture the wound and cauterize until it is healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a damsela took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channel of the windpipe; and I was called to perform the cure, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood issuing from it. I knew she had not cut a vein or any other major artery, as the blood was coming from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened,缝合了伤口，并彻底治愈了她； damsela的voice并未受损，很快恢复了正常；因此我敢说，在治疗咽喉疾病时无需恐惧。
de la grosse gorge	of the main throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color like that of a hazel nut, and it is very common in women; and it occurs according to two manners: natural and accident; or naturally there is no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs according to two manners, of which one is similar to fatty tumors, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from within the artery; and there is fear, and it should not be operated on by making openings except in that which is small, and the probing and searching must involve all the intervening areas: if you find it as fatty as we do, and cannot be distinguished from any vein, then cut it out as one cuts fatty tumors, and draw it to its entire core if there is any; and search thoroughly at once, and cure it as fits until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways we have, of which I will say all the likenesses; and now it comes that I must say all the difference there is between us and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever lasting until the boiling has passed, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the shoulder having no heat, fever, or pain, and containing the syphix, which is its own sack and according to the color of the body, it begins like a swelling, and becomes large; and are according to two likenesses, or fat, or moist, and much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It must be, when you come to the treatment of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "intromissory", according to what its form will come or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you probe or find a softer part of the lump of the abscess, and turn your two probes little by little, until you know that the instruments have reached the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intromissory instrument, and be careful in this that it does not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs clear or of any other color, cut it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after extracting the intromissory instrument there is no further moisture, know that it is fatty, so cut it crosswise, and take it out with forceps, and gently scorch each part. Guard the cloth where it lies, and treat it soundly with the wound; and if you cannot treat it soundly whole, remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there is nothing, it returns to us many times; and if there remains a little, and the wound grieves, fill the wound with some corrosive powders and fluids, hold the wound, and apply warm abscess-soothing things on top, and cure it with other cures until it heals; and if the wound is large, suture the two edges of the wound, and cure those who require flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beating is against you or another thing hastens it, use the juice of pounded vitriol, and let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound rots, and rest the boiling of the blood; then return to copper that which has remained from the new one.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the intervening instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small. Among them are three square ones called "albaret," and one called "breb." There are also three kinds of these instruments: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses from fistulae. They are like the needles used for suturing threads, made of yellow copper or iron or silver. The yellow ones are more effective than black ones for encircling corruptions from fistulae. They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the canine teeth are similar in appearance, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and among these canines there are those with two corners in three ways; and among them are canines with three corners, and are also in three ways; and among them are canines with two corners, and only one corner, and are in three ways; and all of this are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief part of what is done are the incisions, and among these there are those that cut only half-way, for which we cauterize the edges, because one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and from these introductions are the alembics placed in channels, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they come in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and no force is used except in firm parts such as legs, arms, mammary glands, and angles, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling shells of nuts, according to this form, for cauterizing blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed once where the wound heals by degrees from the veins, and in the arteries, and once they follow according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Once the breasts of some men swell when they begin to腐坏，直至似乎变成女人的乳房；并且remain ugly and swollen; and whoever needs to treat them should do so according to this form of line .b. from .g. :
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then cauterize the fat, and apply the wound with a healing salve, then suture the two edges of the wound together, and treat it until it heals. And if the breast hangs down and becomes soft due to its size as in women, cut it between the two ribs above, following similar incisions; ensuring that one edge is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the minor according to this form, from line .b. to the line .g.; then cauterize the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and administer as we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the discharge of blood, you should fill the wound with moist cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of swellings
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the swellings are forms of hard scrofula with nodes, and among them there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be lanced according to this form, from the line 2 to the line 7:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowe that is in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment appropriate for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are of the appearances of scrofula, lance them as we have said for the incisions in scrofula. And if the wound contains bowe, apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn shut, many abscesses often develop. The same occurs with a swollen vein and an abscess; if one recognizes this for an arterial rupture, the abscesses grow long and large; and when you feel it with your hand, you sense the tension; and when it is due to a vein, it appears as swelling in the veins; and it is foolish to attempt to treat such an abscess, especially when it is near the armpits, angles, and around the collarbone and many other areas, and is very large.
