Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one should avoid the iron cure. For him who is in chief pain, it is also advisable to avoid this method. In those swollen from arterial rupture, make a cut above the skin long enough; then operate the incision with forceps, and cleanly separate the artery from the tissues until it is fully exposed. Place an awl under the skin, piercing it through to the other side, and tie the artery with double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples. Then insert a piece of cloth between the two threads at the point where they meet, allowing the fluid to drain from one side to the other; thus, release the abscess. Continue this treatment until the threads separate. Use ointments appropriate for these conditions until it is healed. If the abscess is due to vein swelling, you must apply your hand and squeeze out as much of the abscess as possible onto the skin. Place an awl under the thread you are holding with your hand, pierce through, and use double thread to ensure thorough drainage. Once the fluid has drained, treat the excess skin and leave what is tied. Then place a moist cloth in wine and oil, and continue with bandages and ointments until it is fully healed.
des apostemes des ners	from abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses coming to the artery and to the vein, abscesses of nerves when they are injured, or through too great labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more frequently in joints and in all places where there are articulations, and it is the grief of abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and is in many dispositions with pain; and when one restrains it forcefully, the patient feels great pain, and it is not just painful throughout the body, but beneath the heart; and it moves well in all directions, neither forward nor backward, neither below nor above, and that which is in joints should not be treated with iron: by chance there might be a contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead causes the skin to rupture at the temple.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and squeeze at its root; and if it is large, suspend it by a thread, burn it, then remove it and suture the wound, treat the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large blisters hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	In no case does it occur in the belly or anywhere else on the body; it is a disease called "fungus" by its similarity to mushrooms. The roots are fine and the heads large; some are small and others quite large. I have seen a man who had two bellies that looked more like mushrooms than anything else, with no difference between them, and they were white, had small roots, and were jagged, and there was moistness in them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces, and in the other VI [pounds], and in the work of incision it is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the arterulus is white and moist and of subtle root; so cop it with large spatumile, and let the cautery be at fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the tailoring, there are often too great outflows of blood, and if the patient faints, you must then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient terrified and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made plonc thread, and tie the arterulus as we have said, and let it be two days; and then release, and do not cease to strain the plonc thread until it copes the arterulus, and work carefully through it; and if the roots are large, you may fear to cut directly for the belly, but you can well cut the half of them, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cut the thernel which is of fugue color and poor sense and looks like milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an embedded abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is hot
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a fire cautery on a wound or a cut in the skin, and it is on the belly and some of the boils, as happens in other wounds, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from wind; and if it is due to the rupture of the skin and the discharge of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and is a mild thing without pain, and obvious with various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge from the intestines, then it is more varied, and when pressed at its base it rises and then returns, and sometimes it swells and greatly enlarges upon entering the bath and through much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and clearly apparent when you press it with your hand; it does not constrain much. And if it is due to blood, it is clearly shown by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and inserted in a certain quantity. And if it is due to phlegm, it is cold to the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery, or a vein, or phlegm.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the treatment proceed.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery or vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the boil, you must instruct the patient to stretch his arm and lie completely straight, then draw it all around the mouth; then command him to lie very still between your hands, then go down to the place where you have drawn the sign for the entire circumference, then place half of the abscess above at the top of the large inch; then tie it together with a strong thread or a rope of fine silk tightly, and let it be fixed in this manner; then work the other half of the abscess stretched over the thread, and use your index finger to hold it; if you find it caught on the thread, release it, and allow the intestine to escape through the abdomen; and if you find the boil, take it with the inch, and drain the excess; and if the artery makes it contrary or the vein, go in properly, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strands of thread, and insert the needles into the cross where you made the piercing; then pull the abscess through four turns over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and cut out the dead flesh by itself; or you drain it when it is fine and rotten, then treat the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place with what is appropriate, and close the wound.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the signs of the chancre, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how one must avoid iron cure; and we say that the chancre arises in the groin, and great caution is needed in its treatment. The ancients said that when chancres are found where they can be scraped off, like those on the sameles [thighs], and in similar places, and should all be removed when they are at the beginning; but when they are large and old, it does not matter to approach them, for I have never seen any heal from them, nor has anyone healed from them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is found where one can remove it, as we have said, are that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him sweated if he has evident distension, then shave the patient well in the place for the operation; then throw out the tumor or chancre, and all the hair from all parts, removing everything without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely, and wipe the place with your hand or something else thoroughly, and if the bleeding continues contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize until the blood has stopped; then treat it with other remedies until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already spoken of the signs of dropsy and how the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each sign, and the cure through medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is only clarified; and one must not use iron in these two signs: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because they are deadly things; therefore, when you treat this sign of dropsy called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not help, look if the patient is weak or has another illness besides dropsy, such as an immediate solution of the belly and similar things; in these cases, do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient full of virtue, and he has only dropsy and is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus: lift the patient straight up with your hands, and the attendants press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the spatumile thorny according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let the point be cut in two parts, and let it not be inserted too deeply so that it cannot reach the intestines when thrust in, nor be blocked; then look to see if the hydrocele is near the intestines: if this is the case, you must cut through from beneath the scrotum three incisions over the point of the knife; and if the hydrocele is due to liver disease, make your cut on the left side of the scrotum three incisions; and if it is due to the spleen, make them on the right, and it must not be that the patient lies on the cut so that the superfluous fluids do not flow to the weak part; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, empty it, and withdraw your hand, leaving a small passage between the skin and the scrotum as if scraping with the quantity of a nail or slightly less; then pierce the scrotum until the fluid appears at that site, which is the outlet for the water, then extract, and use this instrument whose form you know.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver needle, made of light brass or steel, and used near the part beneath the small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision that writers cut the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	On the head above is the alemele, such that when the instrument comes to the edge, it goes down now above the instrument; empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than necessary in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls senseless, or he nears death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to the dispositions of the virtue of the patient that signify, and his pulse; then draw the instrument and hold the edge, and it is held now for the key which stops the hole which is above the syface, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the instrument on another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw a little of the edge; do this any day, and take care not to follow too much until it no longer remains but just a bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water in him, cure it with warm earth or sand, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and let him drink; cure with medicines that dry him up until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping up of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have pores in the urethra, or where the pores are small, or are not in their proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to act promptly before it has pierced all the subtle parts according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then apply or insert a small plug of flax, and secure it and keep it for three days or four; and when it is time to urinate, remove the plug, allow urination, and then replace it; and by chance it may not be necessary at all, as the urine that comes forth does not always leave the plug closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the patient's plug is small, it should be medicated with a cloth of flax, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the plug in their place should be bleached, for none are born with the plug at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis upward; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot reach the rectum, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on their back, then the head of the verge and the cope are made as large as a feather's size, so that the perforations pierce through the middle, as it should; and beware of the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these ulcers come in the verge, and they are an appearance of ugly flesh; and among them there are malignant and non-malignant; so you must treat them with a sharp lancet, and cut and cleanse all, then put on soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and offensive, you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when you have taken it out, and if the ulcer is in the groin and has part inside the skin and part outside, you must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is healed, treat the one outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, it is not assured that the head of the groin will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come into the groin and nearby tissue; you must cut out everything that is black and corrupted, then bandage with a plaster made from the bark of pomegranate peels and vinegar, and treat it with other dressings until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is a bleeding episode, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with the two dispositions together: that is to say, in cases of bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must insert a rod into the penis and let the patient urinate through it. And when the hair is shaved at the head of the penis which comes to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then you must therefore cauterize with a heated instrument over a small part of the head of the penis and the skin; then separate well between them, and apply a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water so that it does not burn again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the opening of wounds like other injuries; yet when we perform this work of our will, and properly for infants, it is necessary that we do the best work and the most gentle for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have none but what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have spoken with the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions using razors, forceps, and even an entire pair of scissors; they would often complain because there are two blades, and by chance one might cut above and the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is copper, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleansing which is from down below, the points of the limb are not assured; and in the cleansing of the nail by accident the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they arise thus without need of cleansing and I have willed this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing which is done at the joints to all the thread of hair I have found the worth of experience, for the joints cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, you cut equally all around; but that the threads be well thin under the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if he hears it, that you are only tying the thread around the shaft just so, and let him see you try in all manners that you can; then hold the shaft straight with your hands, and place the forces between your hands or under your feet where the child cannot see them nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the shaft and blow or kiss it, and draw it up until the heads of the shaft are out; then cleanse well from the filth that is gathered, then tie the upper signet with a double thread, then tie under each link one by one; and hold at two doings in the second hour at the pouchet and the right index, and sew between the two links, then remove the keur quickly above and draw the head of the shaft; then let the blood run little by little, for it is the most painful; and put powder on and over the powder a glued wick of a half egg cooked until the water rose, confited with rose oil well and fresh, and let it be on until another day, and cure with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of force for the ceremony is this: the two shoulders should be strong and sharp, and the shoulders should be as large as the thighs equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the ceremony is when the openings inside do not reach the incision; therefore, you must extend it with your nail, just as the teeth make an abscess; and keep it even, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, hold it with forceps, and then press.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass for three days, and that which is beneath the foreskin is swollen, let it be until the abscesses have subsided, and gently scorch it; and move it as you can, and keep away from the part of the foreskin, as it will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the limb of sudden wounds from powder, as we have said in treating powders, and if it swells beyond measure, it will not harm; cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	for retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	For the retention of urine, it is due to stone passage, or congealed blood, or bowels, or flesh that has come forth, or similar things as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released and you see the retention due to a stone at the mouth or neck of the bladder, then the patient should be instructed to bend their knees; and the feet should be placed on the back, and extend their belly from the part above the back, and constrain the patient so that they can bend as much as they can; and thus, the neck of the bladder is forced to express the stone upwards, for which reason the urine is released. And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which here is its form: and it should be made of fine silver, light and slender like a bird's feather; and let the handle be one and a half palm long, and let it be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie at the head a little bit of wool or cotton, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess of the wool and put it until the head of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and the penis with moistened oil and olive oil and water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, as much as it comes to the root of the penis, then cover the head of the penis above towards the mouth; then insert the syringe forward until the bladder, and let the patient feel the urine coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order because those who conduct or where it goes are crooked; then remove the thread little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make the urine flow; and continue the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and bind the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come to the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled, and you see it discharge acidic fluids and medicines, then use the instrument called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see. The leashes are attached so that the medicines may be well absorbed by the bladder, inducing a good numbing effect. Thus, moisture can be drawn out when necessary, and poured back in when needed. When you see your medicines flow into the bladder, place the tip of the tube in the moisture, then draw it out slowly. This will draw the moisture from the bladder to the tube, and then you should firmly pour it back into the bladder; this way, the moisture enters again and is felt by the patient, now that the diseased part can sense it. And this is the form of the fine catheter used to treat the bladder: as shown here.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of copper, and the head is higher; and below at the breast where the fluids fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you see to moisten the bladder in it, then tie between the two breasts forming a thick double thread, and heat that part of the moisture over the fire; then insert the chief of the clyster into the vagina, then draw your hand over the bladder until all the moisture is evenly applied, so that the patient feels that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly through; then insert the strong thread in these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles the parts of the die, and put inside what you want of liquid and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture is applied to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken of the divisions of stones and their extraction along with medicines; and we have mentioned the difference between a stone embedded in flesh and all its signs, and which stone one should operate on by size; and concerning the bladder and the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine has changed in its subtlety, seeming like water; it frequently irritates the child's penis, and causes pain many times, and then becomes more severe; most of these jumps are in the foundation. And the healing of children is light until they are four years old, and is very serious in the elderly, and is moderate for those between childhood and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have larger stones than for those who have smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a clyster to remove all the filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it obstructs sometimes in seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and stretch and move them out, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and exits once from above; then place him in a position suitable for you, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder hangs entirely downward; then hold it and touch it internally; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to incise over the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not descend upon touching from the entire length, soften your index finger of the left hand, if the patient is in pain, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young adult; then move your hand to its foundation, hold the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, amass at the neck of the bladder; then press above your finger, and incise where you see fit.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch his right hand upward, and remove the skin beneath the coccyx in the part where the incision is made; then he pours in the spatumile cutting, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make the incision between what is between the coccyx and the pelvis, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight above the stone, and your two hands should be near the foundation or pelvis, and the incision should pass through so that it is wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, pressing may make the hand at the foundation jump out easily; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: they are easier to remove; and some are underneath, resembling a groove and round, from which the removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have angles and margin, make the size greater; and if it does not fit, you must clamp with tongs that are like a file at the head, to move and extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under the delicate curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot contrive it thus, you enlarge the hole slightly, and if the surface is uncured, you extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, you put the larger one first at the neck of the bladder, then cover up, then pull hard, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must sew it up, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out through him where the bones cannot close; but nevertheless strive to treat it, or to extract with tongs piece by piece until you have completed your work. Then dress the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly with a wet cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the inflamed abscess; then re-wrap the patient on his back, and do not untie the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, you should raise much well the head of oil and water, then treat with a salve of definnic and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions come into the wound and clots of blood in the bladder, and thereby urine is retained, which is known to be in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: pour then your urine into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder; then wash the wound with water and grease and salt, and aid it in all ways that you see until it is healed; and it must be that for all wounds you cure, you tie the two thighs and apply the medicines to the head.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is located in the passage of the penis, and stuck there, and urine cannot pass; you should cut as I said before, but this cutting can be excused due to the need for urination.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this in such a manner.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron rods according to this form and fix them at three angles in the fire:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the penis over the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the iron rod gently into the penis until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron rod in the stone little by little, as much as you can pierce the stone from another side; then urine will come forth soon. Then press your hand above what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken soon, and its fracture is with urine, the patient recovers; and if you cannot do this for any reason, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then make the probe at the stone between the two threads, extract it forcefully, untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that the stone of women is incarcerated, and if it happens even once, it must be carefully cured, and is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that by chance the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who can disclose herself to examination, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art with her hands; and the fourth manner is that the woman’s stone is more prominent than the man's, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear comes from it. And if necessity rises to these, it must be that you seek a midwife well knowing, and find her among the women there, and if you do not find one, at least get a clever midwife; and present before them a safe woman in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command about the inquiry of the stone; and look very well that the woman is a virgin: then she must use her right or foundation, and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she must compel her under her right, and recommend to her that she uses her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it greatly from the entrance of the bladder until over, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the knee, prepare where it will be moved open, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and let the cut be at first small; then press the wick into the cut, if you sense the stone enlarge the wound as much as the stone can exit forth, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with grooves.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the signs to know the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the sinew breaks, put vitriol powder on it and keep it for an hour until the sinew is healed; then return to your work while the stone is being extracted, and have with you the instruments I told you about in the extraction of the stone for those who help you in your work; and if the sinew breaks, and this is from the artery that has been cut, put powder on it and bandages, and do not attempt to reset it again, leaving the stone untreated, lest the patient die suddenly; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the swelling has gone down, then return to your work while the stone is being extracted.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous humor is nothing but a collection of moisture or white fluid, which is outside the heart of the eye, containing the egg; and it is called "syphac," and sometimes properly within the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it is another egg. And this is the skin of the eye between the white fluid we have said; and it does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this aqueous humor is due to weakness that comes to the eyes, and this material is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the eyes, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a color declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more often; and these are the signs to recognize this collection, because if it is the white fluid we have said, it is the sign of well-formed abscesses, somewhat long like the figure of an egg, and does not protrude from the eyes, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the proper membrane, the abscess is incised with a part of the egg, and because of this, one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the quill and the white shell, one senses it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you prove it through the intervening square, as its form is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intervening square, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we incise it with iron, the patient must be bled according to our power and the fullness of his body; then sow on his back, above something slightly high, and put much flax over him; sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, extending the needle to one of the two ribs of the quill of the coion; then take the leaden spatula, and cut the skin of the coion among them long until near the knife, and let the incision be straight by dividing the skin of the coion up to the white shell, and cauterize subtly according to your power; then pierce the white shell full of water through a large hole, and drain all the water out, and then put your pins, and set the white shell upward; and do not touch the quill of the coion, but only the white shell; cut completely or in pieces himself evenly subtly, that if you do not cut it well sagaciously, the water will return; and if the egg should burst during your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the shell; then join the two flaps of the quill of the coion with a seam, then treat it as other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspensive, suspecting the bleeding; then cut the cord completely at the suspensive part, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the abscess is assembled in two parts joined together, know that these are two branches; cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood and put oiled wool in the wound; and place another moistened wool in wine and oil, and put above the two cords, and put underneath doubled cloth, and tie it all according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded wool according to this likeness, and sew them together at the waistband of the trousers. One head of the shoulder is placed from the fundament up to the back, and the other on the part of the armhole; and the other two heads over the two angles, and tie all the straps in the loop of the trousers. This branch is often treated with a fire cautery instead of iron clamps, and you should use a sharp surgical cautery to burn through the skin flap containing the abscessed fluid. Then take the cautery according to this form, and prick that skin flap with the points, and brand it with the sharp hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the coagulum in all ways that you can, until you are dry; and guard that the fire touch not the egg; and know that this work is more perilous; and use guarding from bleeding, and make sure that the cuts are clean; and if anything contrary to you happens, or abscesses, or hemorrhage, or other things, cure what makes contrary to you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, administer perforation as I have told you. When you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that watery abscess is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the area below with a wide lancet, and place the perforation lengthwise along the body; let the openings be large so that all the fluid may drain. Then put cotton over the wound and bind it, allowing the remaining fluid to continue to drain, and cure the wound until it is healed. If the white cloth does not allow the fluid to exit through the opening of the wound, you must insert a feather or the instrument used for draining dropsy fluids, as described earlier. Widen the opening of the wound, and know that the fluid will return and gather after about six months or so; when it has gathered as before, the patient's days will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In this section there is much to fear in various disposals, which makes it seem to me that one should avoid it if possible; and I will tell you the work and similar matters of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the body, and especially from the joints; and this is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say that they come from bitter and acrid superfluity, which spreads to the joints, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the body; and it does not find any pain, and is a grievous abscess; and by chance it may be a grievous and stony abscess, and of fugitive color, and sometimes comes from a vein, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess; when you press with your thumb and index finger; and it should not be touched at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which is caused by vein swelling is known by its arrangement at the expression of the touch of the thumb and index finger, and can well be cut on this appearance and on the other marks; and you must take the heart out of the veins, then set the yolk on top, and let the white stretch downward, and release the suspender from all sides of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the yolk is already hardened with these marks, then you must cut the yolk and the heart; and if it is airy at the bottom or within the veins, then you must release all that is contained, and roundly take out the heart.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birthplace of the flesh is open behind, it must be cut entirely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, apply the wound with moistened wool in rose oil and wine, then treat with other dressings until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a borjon, with the groin area softened. The patient experiences pain as it fluctuates; and the treatment for this disease must be thoroughly performed as described earlier, and we will detail the work according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must seat the patient on an elevated chair, then place the suspensory ligament of the groin below your knees, over all the vessels near the thigh, and tie them firmly; then cut with a sharp spatula through the traversing veins until they are uncovered, and then cauterize from each part as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then insert a needle where it has the double thread, and attach it to the first knot where the vein entered, and reattach at the other end; then cover in the middle straightly according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures; then treat the wound as with others where one inserts bowe, so that no vessel breaks which nourishes one of the coions; for by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels are pierced, it is necessary to remove from all the vessels; so that the eye does not lose its nourishment due to incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be healed.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the throat
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are due to the section that comes from the throat or the extension in the abdomen in the part of the flanks, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the coxae; and this rupture is either of the throat or from the extension thereof, and come from these two kinds of causes: by percussion, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs when it is due to the extension of the throat, are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal until near the surface, because the throat presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is due to the section of the throat, that it causes an sudden onset of pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear varied, beneath the skin near the surface, and this is due to the discharge of the intestines and the core behind the throat.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the veins with the intestines are affected, and they remain inflamed, and cause great pain to the patient, especially when they are compressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these burns from iron, for which it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of this work is that you command or instruct the patient to warm the intestines in his hand from within the wound, if they can fit inside; then bandage it around his neck, between your hands, and lift the thighs. Then place the keur above, and scrape all the skin from the long coions; then insert the leivers of the taille uncines according to what you need to open the wound, making sure that the oes can exit; then cauterize the syface which is below the skin from the long coions, until the white syface becomes hard visible on all sides. Then insert your index finger into what follows the coion, between the white syface which is below the skin of the egg, and between the second syface, and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second syface; and then move with your right hand inside the keur from the coions, and place the white syface on top in your left hand, and lift the egg towards all the syface towards the taille. And command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and untie what is air behind the ligament.
