Wait with your fingers if there is any intestine enveloped or hard white syface, and if you find anything, put it back into the belly under it; then take an awl that has a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it in the rear part of the syface, which is after the skin from the coions; behind the taille, then scrape the heads that appear from the threads until there are four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other like a cross, and secure the syface, about which we have said is below the skin from the coions, with a strong thread from two sides. Then wrap the heads of the threads, and secure them firmly from two sides, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter outwards, so that the abscess does not come back; then reinsert the thread according to the first long thread for two fingers, and after these two threads leave the syface which is below the keur from the coions the size of a thumb; then continue all around according to the roundness that the egg carries. Then scrape in the part which is below the skin from the coions until it is clean, and the bowels, as we have said before; then administer moistened wool and place it on the wounds, and give the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the whites of the eyes are cauterized to prevent hemorrhage after incision due to doubt.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leave the thread until it falls by itself; and if it delays in falling, it should be removed with hot water, and then apply what we have said until it falls; then treat the wound with other dressings until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnosa
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the threads that are woven together by a weaver, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after lightly cutting the hernia; then cut it in half, and treat the abscess of him who works, until the vessels heal; and treat it as we have said until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes there is a rupture in the groin, as we have said, and the testicles become apparent; and no parts of the intestines protrude through the wound, but if they do, it is only a little and return every hour; and still, if it remains too long at this point, the wound becomes infected or syphax, until the intestines protrude; and this happens due to the extension of the syphax in the groin, as we have said, because it extends, then softens and swells the testicles and the wound opens; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have already said; and sometimes the wound is treated with a iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then take the swollen testicle of the rupture and enlarge the hole according to the size of three fingers; then extract the syphax which is beneath the skin that follows, then place the flax and put it over the apparent testicle; and press it well against the belly, then suture the two apparent testicles above the head of the flax, and suture both; then extract the head of the flax, and do not cover or extend the wound or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ramification of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The flax is constrained, and shows no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterizations are healed in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the knees
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the knees is softened in some people because the flesh within is softened, and it is to be seen. When one wishes to treat it, one must lay the patient prone on their back, and cut away the soft skin above the natural skin. Then join the two edges with a single stitch, and if you see fit, sew the excess of the soft skin with three or four stitches firmly. Afterward, cut between the stitches and treat the wound as other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	by due correction
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Such correction is prescribed in our law, and since I find it fitting that I not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary for two reasons: one is that you may know how to respond when asked about it and know its treatment; and the other, because we often have need to correct certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cattle, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that corrections are made in two ways: either by attraction or by splitting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by attraction, place the beast in hot water until the joints become soft and relaxed. Then grasp them with your hand while they are thus restored and you no longer feel any pain.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castrating a bull: you must brand the beast, and press the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut above each ovary one time when you have well scalded them; and leave some of the fatty substance and the fine fatty substance that is under the vessels; and this method of castration is better than that done by attraction, because in attraction there remains by chance something from the testicles, which causes the beast to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are according to two manners in men: one is that between the two testicles it appears as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in the middle there is urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and it is done with a knife as a rod and two pegs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you clean all the set bones, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for those whose urine flows through the skin of the pegs, it does not require any treatment.
de la tentigene	of the wart
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A wart is a set bone on the natural part, such that it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is how they are treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to dye the excess of the wart with your hand or needles and treat it gently; and do not apply too much, lest blood flow, then treat it with other remedies until it heals. And for another bone that arises at the mouth of the vein, fill it and sometimes it may burst, and it resembles a cow, hence they called it in ancient times "kowee disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to extract it, as we have said about the tumor and its treatment, and continue the cure until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratum
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the perforation is small; and it is natured by birth, or an accident caused by illness that comes about; or it is through artificial means, or a thin or thick syphon, and is made perfect in the liver, or in the flanks, or below, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and sometimes flowering to have; and the knowledge of this is by the gaze of the midwife.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppages are close and apparent, seek help with your fingers or the rag.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle sore and near the two flanks, hasten, and proceed thus: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two flaps, as much as the subtle sore requires, and place them over the stumps; then take wool, and fat in oil, and apply it to the flesh, and let the woman lie on her side each day, so that it does not heal too quickly.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sore is hard and thick, it is necessary to apply several layers of lint resembling leaves of bay.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stumps are of flesh born, suspend them with a pin and a cop; and have the blood-stopping medicines, such as myrrh, dragon's blood, incense, together with plenty of egg; then apply a wide strip of lint, so that the wound does not heal; and thus leave it long, and give him another linen tent to dry; then continue to treat with other treatments until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is abscessed pus in the boil, you must treat it according to this method, unless it is an embedded abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the embedded abscess in the boil, one must not touch it to incise.
des emorroides	for hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without core (intake) usually occur frequently. And when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into warts; and I have already described similar cases in the division of symptoms, and their signs, and now I will describe those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and warts, when fully inflamed in the boil, do not appear by sight, except for those cured with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the boil, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold room, then put the gall-bladder in its roots, and sprinkle medicines that restrain blood, such as myrrh, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then press her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and the bark of pomegranate peels and galingale and similar things, and then take wheat flour, mix it with honey and garlic, and apply it as a poultice to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, if they cause suction cups to be applied to the back and breasts without piercing; then take wool, and the fat in the juice of plantain or in the juice of agrimony with old wine, and apply it there.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so you should treat it as I said for the thigh; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the armpit
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the armpit, such as chancre, pierous abscess, herpes, estiomenes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must say in this treatise on the hot abscess that comes from the armpit, which is not among those abscesses that swell like boils; and if you wish to know the ironwork, observe whether the abscesses are hard at the beginning of their appearance, and full of heat and fever, and become red if you can see them.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce but let it die until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on the seat, and have two small seats or cushions for him to recline, supporting his back and aligning his feet with the parts below the leg; and spread his thighs, and place his arms beneath his knees, and bind them tightly with a good bandage; then apply the bowl to the right side, and bring it to the location where the mouth of the armpit is made, from which the form will come later; and it must be that when you see this instrument being administered, you insert the needle first to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not injure the patient; and if the instruments are larger, it must cover the depth of the armpit with cloths, so that the instrument does not weigh on him; and it must place the horn of the instrument above, and touch the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened, and it is made soft by hand, you must cover it at the head, in the spatumile leak; and when the bow is emptied, you must put moistened cloths in rose oil, or in green vitriol oil; place the end of the cloth over the sore and above the knife on a clean moistened cloth in water or honeyed wine that has been cooked; then cure after two days with ointment suitable for this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the sore and the wound by enema with water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and long pepper that have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed over the sore, you must take care not to use iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The craft is first in labor when she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing downward, and desiring to urinate: then hasten the birth; thus know that this birth follows its natural figure, issuing with its head, and the second follows with it; and when you see these signs, you must gently press her abdomen, so that the child comes forth quickly; for when it descends on its head, the second follows with it, and is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing. And who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes on its feet, and comes forth through the body or the shoulders, and the hands, or it comes through the abdomen or loins, and is turned by chance over its neck, and by other evil figures; therefore it is necessary for labor that she be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes to his head naturally, and the woman gives birth easily, and the virtue of her is weak, then place her on a seat, or hold her; and from its nature, take oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then put the mixture between her two small labia as they are formed.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the secondine, and take off as much as its moisture is expelled; and press the woman's abdomen until the child descends. If it does not descend, then cleanse the woman with fenugreek muscilage and olive oil; then make her drink and sneeze with condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands protrude, you must reset them gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet high; then raise the seat to the ground, and support the woman so she does not move during the extraction; and if the hands cannot enter and the child has died, cut the hands with the knife mentioned earlier, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child above his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the infant comes above its feet, one should lift it up; then turn it little by little, until it is even; then straighten the legs and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump as far as the knees, instruct it to stretch, and make it sneeze by coughing; if it jumps, let God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to natural alignment.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly aligned.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not jump as we have said, take a muscled althea bark, and silk worm's eye, and melted gum, and grind them all in the mortar; then apply this ointment to the woman's nature, placing it beneath. Have her sit in warm water until below the ribs; when she is softened below, place a myrrh collar over her, and put it under, and let her remain for an hour; then have her sit on the seat, and make her sneeze while holding her mouth and nose, and gently rub her abdomen, for the infant now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue from the child above its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child takes this form, gently place its hands little by little; then bind it on its neck, and let its feet hang down, and lie down on the bed; bend its hands little by little, and then place its hands on its belly, and remove the cushions under it until it is prepared to come down; and if the child does not cry, take its feet and move them into shape, then move its belly upwards, then put your hands in; and slowly pull the child; and command the woman to support it as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child that comes wide with one hand hanging
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must devise to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make her stand and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her down on the bed, and prop up her legs. Then administer the ligature as I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the seat, then strive to bring back the hand; and turn the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to grip until the infant is delivered.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child at its neck, and have spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I must have the midwife grasp the child's hand, then turn it little by little and gently; and when it is aligned, place the ligature of thread and oil, as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and command her to grip; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to all the secondine in this manner, scrape the secondine with your nail until the moistors are evacuated; and if the pains can be felt on her face and on her neck, scrape from the cleft, do not retain it, and end the pains; then put the child inside, as soon as you have placed it properly, and instruct the woman to push once: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the extraction of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born often, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not strange, nor does it happen rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are extracted and do not live much, if at all; I know these, that they be multiplied, and are deprived by the syphilis which devises them, which is linked to the bowels; and sometimes sent naturally as if they were many undergrowths, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out properly, the treatment as we have said, and let the bile be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do so as it is worth to contribute to healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of the glorious sage, and it must be that the bile know all this, for similar things may happen; do so according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the mother of the dead child or abdomen, as I have said in the division, and there is no discharge, and you are forced to perform manual operations; you must know whether the woman is of sound health and has no accidents or fear of death; the woman should be soothed on her back, with her head inclined forward, and her legs raised; the minister should support from two sides, tying her to the bed so she does not move during the descent of the child; then rub the mother's mouth with moist oil mixed with muscilage of ale and fenugreek and linseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and muscilages; gently insert the fingers into the mother’s anus, then remove them in a manner suitable for the situation, ensuring that the child is prepared to descend on its head; if the descent is through the feet, insert or puncture at the middle of the back; it must be ensured that the first dose goes to her right hand, and place the cord between her left index finger; she should gently apply this to all her fingers, inserting the dose into any of the places we have mentioned until it reaches an empty spot; this is the form of the dose:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then drive it against the other awl, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions be equal; and then stretch equally by moving back and forth, to allow them to come out, and let the awls have teeth to hold them, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, open with any of his eye teeth, and push it into that part, and cut the other part; and if there remains nothing, set this awl or higher up, and do this until all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by gripping, then you must wrap it with a cloth, until all comes out; then fold it at the joint of the sole or on the cut, and thus you must do in the other hand, and with both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and the birth passage is narrow, or if there is a sharp protrusion, then you must insert the pointed spatula between your fingers, make the cut, and extract the sharp protrusion; or you may use an instrument called "almidach", which comes with the tools or chapter after this one; and thus do the same to cause the child to naturally pass through a large opening; and then pull the bones with tongs, and if the head suddenly becomes dislocated and is forced into position, split it until the moisture that has entered comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the abdomen or below the back, then you must pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the injury is on his feet, the traction is light, and the direction to the mouth of the vein is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or on the breast, it is necessary to extract it with an inflated bandage wrapped around the hand; and make an incision in the belly or the breast, as much as the fluids that are there permit; and if the other limb has been removed, and the head remains, he should apply his hand thoroughly to the mouth of the vein, and draw it until the mouth of the vein; then he should apply one or two ounces, and draw firmly; and if the mouth of the vein is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, it is not necessary to work on it, but it is necessary to administer moist and greasy things; and he should apply poultices, and a compress in water softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the injury is on his side, and you can place it even, then administer what we have said for the living child; and if one cannot do so, then use forceps to realign, leaving nothing of the second attempt.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said for the abscesses that come in the loins, and if bleeding occurs, it should be placed in cold water restraining, and continue with other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had died, then缝合了另一个，使第二个也死去。
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed in the mouth, and swelled so much that it opened, and began great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, and I thought long, and could not staunch the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and from it came some bones, and after some days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled much, for the abdomen has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I treated the wound, and found bones in her abdomen, until the woman was much improved; and the woman lay there long thus, and had just a little blood from it; and I recollected this chapter only because when masters find a strange thing, they must know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After comes the form of the presser, to which the books refer; and to two turns of the shoulders of the limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Therefore, the horns should be finer than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth be two fingers wide, and the margin one finger in thickness, and long a palm and a half. Between the two limbs, there should be two adjustments of the same wood, firmly fixed on both ends, each half a palm long or a bit more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, finer and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of pliers; and have two adjustments at the shoulders, as you see, a palm long and two fingers wide. When you wish to open the marrow with this entire instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then insert the two adjustments together into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then work your hand on the entire instrument as you did with the pliers equally, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the marrow until the blade does what it wills.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is entirely mounted, and its appearances are multiplied; and when the mirrors have been arranged, it is more rapid in its work, and higher for men because of its quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not wish to use the instrument, make sure you have arranged it, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to grip her hand, and then administer a snuff of condisi, and hold her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she convulses because of this, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pessary or coverlet, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the patient, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, may be cooked or placed in water on fire. Then put a tube or pessary into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the patient, and hold it until the vapors enter the patient. Then administer snuff as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint moves quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not yet healed, command the maid to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or musk oil, and then place her hand in its natural position, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straight, so that the muscle does not wrinkle during the extraction; but you must move it lightly from side to side, and then cut; it will come and loosen.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the muscle is greatly narrowed, we have already mentioned the treatment for sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, then guard against treating it improperly. But you must tie what is at the mouth of the muscle to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with tetrapharmacon ointment; she will take it and be healed. But still, if she takes it and comes upon a bad smell in the stomach and head, and sickens the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If therefore suitable fumigations are needed for it: some of the ancients have proven the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass resembling a cane, and one places the fine end in the nature, and the large heads above the fire; and let the fumigations be upon the coals, and the scab until it is wasted, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but instead have it stopped with a small plug: therefore it is necessary for the baile to pierce that plug in the right place, and not pierce the fundament itself with a sharp awl, and be careful that she does not touch it; then put on wet wool soaked in wine and oil, and cure with ointment until he is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, place or tie a piece of lint, and let it remain there, and be removed when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it must be treated suddenly: it should be cleaned, as we have said for the piece of lint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the fundament are nodules, and grow larger than those that come out of the fundament defying its function, or in the space between two parts, there may be one fistula or multiple; and when this nodule is old, it works, and often contains moisture, like white pus or fine bowels, and sometimes these fistulas are Persian; they are known by those who have them through evacuation or windiness when the patient has an evacuation, and by accident during a passing of a bowel movement.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas penetrate to the bladder, and to the half of the penis; and reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula penetrates to the fundament and not: it is that you place your index finger or probe into the fistula, and insert a subtle needle of brass or iron when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, insert a subtle probe of linen or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no passage of feces or wind or blood, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is infected up to the bladder or up to the urethra, then he urinates, and cannot be cured by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the thigh, the infection comes up to the place; if there are no twists and the location of the pain is clear, then it is likely deep seated, and neither medicine nor immediate application will help; in these infected fistulas, there is no cure other than labor and the vanity of those who attempt them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	For those that are neither infected nor old, with hope of healing through iron, as I have proven, and where the patient lies on their back; lift the legs up to their thighs, and incline the thighs towards the abdomen; then place a tent over them with charcoal or tinder if there are twists, as long as you know where the tent should come to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain deep within the fundament, you should place your index finger there; if you then feel that the tendon has been pierced, know that it is perianal; if no work is done on it, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can well treat some, but this happens rarely. The aid we make, it is to heat the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as was said before; and you pour it hot into the fistula until it comes from the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that these wetted chars are burned, which resemble a bird's feather; and then cure it with ointment moistened in butter until the char is gone, then cure it with healing ointment closing the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus healed; and if the tent passes between, and does not pierce just to the depth which is the foundation, and there between your thumb and the tent a thick covering of flesh or sinew, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering from the heart; cut off the coprolith from the beginning of the fistula, and place something in front of the tent, and cauterize after, until it comes to the top of the tent; and the tent will be delivered, and fall; then remove those fleshly parts that seem like a bird's feather, and let none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound fails and cuts between you and the work, cauterize with fire or medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cauteries of fire, two good things are assembled: that is to say, the burning of these edges cauterized, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then the treatment of wounds moistened with butter or ground cheese, until the eyes release pus, and the edges burned in the pus; then treat the wound with ointments thick with hard charcoal, and they are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not recur.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the point of its foundation and is distant from the body, place your thumb or foundation there and inquire it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the tissue or muscle or edges, or it is ready to perforate, do not have any way that is not based on trust and hope, by administering one of the three methods: or you cauterize as we have said, or you cut down to the bottom, or if you can, place tents and treat as first; and do not go too far from the point, lest you cut through the tissue that holds the foundation, causing involuntary evacuations; then treat, as we have said; by chance it will be healed. Or you remove that cover and clean it once it is cut away from the bottom, or by tent or another pointed instrument; then shave the defective flesh in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and keep the fistula above the foundation: this would be a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are treated in this manner: and it is when you puncture the fistula, and it is located near the foundation beneath the skin, so take a needle perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you wind the thread around twice, and insert the needle with the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perforated in the margin beneath the foundation, then extract the thread from that punctured area, as you would insert your finger or probe; and pull the tip of the thread, and join the two heads together, and hold them against each other, and leave them for one or two days; and hold them together again until the threads cover the gaps between them and heal; then treat the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, make it perforate in all the ways you can, provided it is not already too well formed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to cauterize for the ligature if it is already too well formed, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous spatumile from which we make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not on the other, for that which should not be cauterized, you do not cauterize, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are in two ways: either they are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and they often have blood inside them; some may be in the fundament and at its head. But those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes have a bit of yellowish water or a bit of blood, and have the color of flesh. The treatment for those within the fundament is to instruct the patient to sit out until the fundament allows it, and the threads appear; if you rush, use tongs or your finger to remove them, then cauterize at their roots. If the moisture prevents you from holding them, use a sponge, or a cotton ball, or a piece of flannel; pull them out with your fingers, then cauterize, and dust with some warm powders that serve as a cauterization; or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization, and treat them with other treatments until they are healed. If the fundament cannot release, apply a strong and bitter enema to wash what is within it, so that it may pass openly; when the patient is well, and the threads have come out of the fundament, the treatment is light; you can grasp them with your fingers or tongs, remove them, then treat as we have said until they are healed, and fear surgical incision.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must administer the suturing in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it through a needle, then draw the thread over and make the needle pierce from another side, turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and let them be wide; then tighten the thread firmly, tie the thread, remove the needle, and do so with all the others, leaving one to drain the excess blood; then place a moist cloth in oil of roses or cerate on the foundation, put it down, and command the patient to rest; and leave him until he convalesces, and when they are healed, apply ointment and other treatments until he is fully recovered.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dry the foundation or dressing dryly
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times, dryness of the intestines occurs suddenly, due to natural constraint, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must reset at the point of a spatule or under your nail the skin above, which you do not let moisten; then cure it until it dries as it should; and if it cannot dry, renew the scraping more forcefully than before, until it heals and is scorched; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formice is a small false appearance on the body, and goes very rapidly throughout. And sometimes one finds it cold, and feels like dying from trembling, and comes over all the body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a needle from an goose feather, or a very hard vulture feather, and place that needle on the tremor, so that the red thread encircles the tremor completely; then turn your hand with all the needle until you cover the tremor completely, and put it perfectly, and root out the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a needle of spider silk or iron according to this form, and make it subtle beneath and passing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Not piercing it, for must hold with the thumb and forefinger, and must press. And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the shoulder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	None of the time the shoulder is cast in silver or lead, or in melted iron or small links; and none of the time instruments made from these materials, both small and large, are used according to their size.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those instruments that are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the shoulder, whether small or large, is such that the stomachs are tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it should have a separation or the stomachs are tied as you see, and the shoulder is pierced through; and it has two holes on one side and one on the other. The stomach is placed where medicines are put, either in a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, with one thumb's breadth between each hole. Then insert a strong thread of raw silk twisted ten or so times into each hole, and sew the stomach together like a sheep. When the medicine is inside, tie it tightly with a strong thread in front of the instrument, then cast it; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it gently; then withdraw the ministers' hands together as much as all is visible, then extract the clyster, and raise the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine sees fit to come out, let the fistula be cleansed as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it will be greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize for a belly discharge disease, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is or foundation, or abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is compressed.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division of wound care; now we will speak about hand treatments and medicines according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the joints or places where they are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are from the strike of a stone, and the cut of a sword or knife, or a lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the joints of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with simple wounds of the head, because the chapter on them will come later.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a head injury, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is due to a stone impact or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt an abscess hot: so make it quickly sanguineous from the cephalic vein itself if only little blood comes from the wound, and let the sainie on the contrary from the damaged part; avoid the patient's excessive intake of wine and large foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not become sanguineous, let the flesh be diminished, and do not drink wine nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, only wet cotton in rose oil, or styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not dried by air or powder, the powder that I will say a little later; and if the fire has dried it, put on some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tenting, then join them with suturing, as I will say for wounds of the belly, regarding suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and spongy, and can only be held with a little, then dress it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, like beans, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten skin and it does not affect the bone, then dress it completely, apply a poultice, and then cure it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be staunched without surgery, and cannot be stopped by medicine, then ligate the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: it is that you put this powder which heals as if the arsenic had moistened it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live wax three parts, and mix them finely, and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it dries well and joins all its blood; and then dress it well, and leave it undisturbed if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with only wax, when one does not have incense or the dragon's blood, but let the arsenic moisten the wound.
