Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has changed the wound while it was still fresh, one should not put this powder there; but apply some digested ointments, or pulses of flour of barley made with water and honey until they produce sweat; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other means but to let the cure alone and put nothing restraining on them, for it hurts the nerves and causes them to wither; and put nothing cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but use medicine above, such as boiled wax in soft water, mixed with rose oil, and boiled wool also washed in soft water, and other mine stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, suture and bind it with bandages, then let the cure proceed until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with bowels, puncture or make a larger incision lower down; and if an artery is severed, and bleeding results, sew it up, ligate it, and cauterize it as needed; and if the spinal cord of the throat is severed, or the vessels, and the passage through which the flesh goes is guarded, therefore the meat goes, suture the vessel on the nerve of the throat, and do not touch the throat but place it according to its natural figure; then tighten properly, and let it for a few days, then cure with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, quill it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all that you can, and leave those that you cannot have until the wound rots away, and the discharge is removed; and if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, examine whether from the wound there gushes black blood: then you know that the wound is fatal. If it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put in any powder or cover it up for the blood to fully coagulate and return to the heart, which would kill the patient; but apply an attracting ointment and change it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more. If there will be no spasm, nor evil tremor of the heart, nor deep injuries; and when you see good signs, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure therefore the sores and other treatments until he is healed; and if she cannot heal, operate, then you know that there is an abscess; treat her as we should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse or on the back, treat the one in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, treat with powder; and if it is near the bone and has cut pieces, clean the wound, and remove any foreign objects if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound drain to ease the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, make your judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	For the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the abdomen are great and medium and small; from a large wound, sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, by which there is internal disruption; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one, because we cannot easily put back the intestines once they are cold, as we can if we put them back while still warm; for when the intestines swell quickly upon feeling the cold, they re-enter the body more forcefully, and thus a medium-sized wound may be better, as we properly place the intestines in their correct position with other wounds. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways: the two common stitches happen in the abdominal wall seam, and the seams of other body wounds are also common; but they are more suited to the abdominal wall seam, and I will say each one and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and no intestinal matter is present, and there is nothing difficult to remove, this can be done by one of two methods: either due to the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in a proper manner: moisten a sponge or a cloth with only water, or you can boil it in water with quince and cypress and spice, and cleanse the intestine until the swelling is removed; and once this astringent wine is made, it must be applied to alleviate swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or with cooked mallow and vervain, for these herbs are known to reduce inflammation; if they cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound using the instrument with which hemorrhoids are treated; and the first cure must be applied only after the cut is made, as there should be no unnecessary cutting unless absolutely necessary; and this is the tool for making the incision: so cut inward along the curve and do not sever completely, and observe here the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has protruded, put it back in place according to its natural form in its proper location, if you have the ability, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the part below the abdomen, you must make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the abdomen, raise his head and hips higher than the parts below, and likewise if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, place him such that the severed part is higher than the other; and thus you must manage as I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And for small wounds, use what you have prepared. Have at hand the minister of purses that can hold all the thread in his hand, and sew up the edges; this is the common method of suturing, where you take a needle or more, depending on the width of the wound. Leave some space from the head of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread at that spot. Pierce both ends of the skin with the needles from inside the skin, so that it passes through from one side to the other, then bring together the four ends of the needles in assembly; then pass double thread around the needle from both sides, and assemble the edges of the wound accordingly. Leave some space again, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, without ceasing until all parts of the wound are secured. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, because very fine needles can cut through the flesh entirely, and overly thick ones cannot easily enter: therefore, they should be medium-sized. Do not insert the needles too far into the flesh and skin to avoid cutting the wound before suturing; then remove the needle heads so they do not irritate the patient when sleeping, and place covers or cloths over the needle heads for easy handling, leaving them until the wound heals. This method of suture with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as one needle suffices for a second stitch; this is where you bring together the four ends of the skin and suturing thread on one needle, and when you have pierced these four ends, reduce the needle to the part where you began, doing it in the manner we mend cloth. Leave the thickness of a small coin between each stitch. This suture will last, and I once sewed a wound on someone's abdomen that had been cut by a knife, with the wound being more than a palm wide, and containing intestines two palms long, situated in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestines after twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days, and I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the priest had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and thread from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the heart straight through, leave the tip of the needle on the syphac or sutured area where you have threaded the needle, and let it pierce from another side starting from the inside out. And the meaning of this suturing is that you sew as a tanner would put together hides, leaving the syphac once on one side and again on the other until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen stated precisely, is such that none do it otherwise: they join the two parts naturally and apply one chief thread to another chief, in this manner: insert a needle or chief of silk nearby, and make a single piercing through the skin, leaving both sides of the cut; then turn the needle, and make a piercing from the outside until inside, through the two sides of the cut; and this is the main method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and none testify to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, or there be thread in each; and one must thrust one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds. And know that when the wound is within the belly, the suturing is greater than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound filled with all its blood, as the surgeon has cleansed it, so you put back the intestines and the skin; then set on the powder growing flesh, and if the surgeon has cleansed it, you set on any ointment that is present until the wound heals; stitch the threads, and let the bandages and the medicaments be tied; then cure the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, you put on old cotton soon as it begins to ooze blood, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound makes communication with the principal members, then it is fitting that you moisten linen lightly in tempered heat oil or in rose oil, and place it between the layers, and under the flaps; and if it feels pain or putrefaction within the flesh, and this often happens, then use clistherines of black wine heated, especially if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and pierce from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is torn, and this is due to the weakness of the veins there and the subtlety of the whole body, and its closeness to the nature of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the shoulder jumps from the wound, reset it back as with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned brown or black, then you must tie the part that is black, to prevent blood from flowing, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ties, and place the two heads hanging below the part of the wound up to above for easier extraction when the shoulder falls out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the joint
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are ruptured and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people, for I saw that a nobleman was wounded or his belly pierced by a lance; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became fistulous, and excretions and wind issued from it; I treated it as best I could, and did not cease to dress it until it healed, and the flaps were sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sutured, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and there was no pain at all, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some surgeons said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a manner: take flax thread with large eyes, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on the two edges, so that it clamps its mouth shut; then cover the head, and this remains so that it cannot be untied, then put another thread after in that manner as before, until the wound is completely filled; thus the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head is burnt in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, one can sew the intestine with a fine thread made from the intestine of an animal in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that be most undamaged, then tie it at its head with a thin linen thread twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and stitch the intestine, and tighten it at the rupture; and this method of stitching for worms is not removed but according to the way of hope and faith; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the larger intestines, there is nothing that can be done but with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called "fistula", especially when it is covered and drains slowly.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodation hard and white, where no pain is felt, and it is also covered like the feathers of an eye; and sometimes it drains clearly, and at other times thickly; sometimes little, and at other times enough; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that does not heal and has no flesh, can only be cured by one of the nine causes: namely, through the smallness of blood or corpus; or due to its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and above the edges, which prevents new flesh from growing; or there is too much pus; or the bones are decayed, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine used in the cure is not good; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or due to the nature of the region where digestion is delayed, health is delayed, and it swells naturally; or there are veins or bone: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the medicines for treatment in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it must be that I shall make thee know the cure of fistula which is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the throat, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and so it is such that it affects the principal property of the body part.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of great concern for healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from this source, and you have faith in its cure, and you see it known, take a tent of wax or iron, if the fistula is straight, keep it steady; and if the fistula is curved, search for it with a subtle tent of flax, for flax fibers can bend around the curvature. And if the fistula has openings and you cannot thoroughly search it by means of tents, cleanse it with a purge through one of the openings, as moisture flows from one opening to another and cleanses it; then carefully probe it that you may know whether there is bone or nerve, and is healed properly, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressed upon by your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know its location, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or any of those places I have said, treat it according to what I have said, and remove the foreign matter and corrupted flesh that are within; and then continue the cure until it is healed. And if the fistula is deeply embedded in the correct place, it must be treated thoroughly as much as you can, then put moistened tents in medicated water, and let them fill up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine may corrode the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments with healthy flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, treat it accordingly.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve is not damaged or among the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then let the king remain until all the corruption is removed, then cure the surrounding flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, return to bowing as before: know that you have not gone far enough: so expose and remain until you are at the core, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reverse it; there is no other means but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with tongs, do so with an appropriate instrument; and if there are many bones, extract all of them, leaving none; and if moisture opposes you, and there is neither error nor fear, cut away the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if thou canst not remove them within an hour, apply something corroding to the wound and let it remain until the flesh is corrupted around the bones, then the bones will be lighter; and if it be a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, reset only the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is much of the corrupted part, coming to the marrow of the bone; it shall have to be cut out entirely up to the corruption, and then cure until it be knitted; and I will tell thee of a fistula which came to a man in his leg, so that thou mayest take example and aid in thy work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around XXX years of age, who had pain in his leg due to a cause within the body, such that the matter came to the leg and it became swollen with a large abscess. There was no reason to open it; but the attendants, out of their folly, opened it repeatedly until many matters drained from the abscesses, and it became a fistula, and much corruption came from the pores, filling the body with pus and moisture. Many attendants treated it for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of healing until I was called; and I saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him, and the great corruption that flowed through the pores; and the body of the youth turned red, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some entered against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes sufficiently to discover a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with corruption extending into the inner bone; I saw what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, until what I removed; and began to heal the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not suture it; and then restarted, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuous in the bone, and treated it, and then removed it, and labored to bind the flesh; but I could not do so much that I cut into about a palm's breadth of the bone, which was brought to complete decay, then healed it with medicines; and it was quickly healed and sutured, and no longer needed further work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and out of fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For during the evacuation of bloodletting often occurred, but it was completely healed, and in the place of the bone a hard scar formed, and it was well situated and had no harm nor any adverse effect at all, neither externally nor internally.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a ligature, and draw it tightly over the end of the bone that protrudes, and command someone to extend it upwards; then place another ligature of wool larger than the first ligature around the scar that is near the bone, tightening the end so that you pull the corrupted flesh away from the bone, and expose the flesh at the spot where you wish to treat, ensuring that the bone does not press against the flesh; and place a hot stick or board under the bone to help cure the corrupted flesh; and it should be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and treat it again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover the flesh entirely; then place a coal under it, and after burning from one part to the other through the corruption, let the burning be long enough of the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut out the corrupt part of the joint, and sew the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no old one but by copper; and if the corruption is where a knife of the hand or a knife of the foot, it is very strong that thing, but in any case, you must inquire about that corruption, how it reveals to you; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but such that the vein or nerve do not oppose you; and know that the incision and the cords for coppering these bones are many, according to the structure of the bone and the appearance of the bone, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and because of this, it is necessary to prepare an instrument suitable to each work; and know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of diseases; so think about the tool you need according to what it suits.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder dislocates either from within or from external causes; and when you have treated the corrosion by cleaning with medicines, and it does not benefit, then you must treat that limb until reaching the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient may escape death, or the greater malice from the defect of the limb; and the signs are that the member becomes black, seeming as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption of the limb spreads to other limbs and takes over the whole body; so hasten in treating it, and if it is due to the sting of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar, and the corrosion is on the head of the thumb, then treat it, giving no space for it to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes as far as the hand, one should brace at the joint, so that the corruption does not come as far as the arm; and if it comes to the arm, one should brace with a cord; and if it passes the cord, it is death, and there is no remedy except by the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, one should brace after the other joint; and if it pierces, one should brace the entire pierce; and if it rises in the leg, one should brace at the joint below the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of bracing or fixing the limb is that you tie it above and below, extend some ministers on one side down, and others ministers on the other side up, and you open the flesh between the two sides with a spatula wide enough for the bone to be uncovered; then brace or fix, and put a linen bandage on each side, so that the sinew does not touch the healthy flesh, and bring about another lesion and abscess around the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the bleeding comes when you work, cauterize the limb quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, bind the injured member with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a pious man: he had a darkness that seemed like a burning fire, and this corrosion came first on his toe of the foot, so much that it encompassed the whole foot; and when the doctors saw the corruption, they hastened to cut the foot, and he was healed; long after, the corrosion returned to his toe of the hand, and he came to me, and I applied things reflective after the cleansing of the body, but the corrosion did not cease; and he begged me to amputate his hand, but I would not, because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he might die, for the virtue of a man was weak; and he became desperate all over, returned to his land, and hastened to cut his hand, and was healed; and I did not relate this story except because one should do otherwise if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess arises in the flesh, and stays so long that it gathers a great mass of pus; then it ruptures and drains, and the pus jumps out, leaving the lumps visible as if they were vessels; and the skin above is as thin as delicate thread, and does not drain all the way to the bone or to the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain," and is not called a "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone properly, it is called a "fistula"; and the skin is such that you peel off all the skin around it, especially when it is thin, as delicate thread; and it does not rupture due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have found that the skin will peel off, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it thus: first, examine whether the swelling is large, and the pus within has a foul smell; then prepare an Egyptian medicated enema as follows: take asafoetida, oil of roses, and litharge, all equal parts, and boil them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey. Then, according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and use it to treat the swelling, pressing on the abscess; leave the medicine there for two hours, then remove it by wringing out any excess. Do this several times until the swelling is reduced and the pus is drained; if you do not have this medicine, you can use ashes from vine branches as a substitute: pour water over the ashes, strain them, and use the liquid to treat the swelling until you see that it is well cleaned. If the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, use a mixture of water and honey with a small amount of litharge; or you can mix honey and wine, where the honey has purifying properties and the wine helps the abscess drain; when you have done this, and if you believe that the swelling is thoroughly cleaned, treat it with a salve that promotes flesh growth. Use oil of roses and wine to prepare it. Or use various medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned or discussed in treating ointments. If the abscess in the breast is small and the enema canister cannot reach it, enlarge it slightly with a sharp object, and place an Egyptian ointment tent or basilicon ointment over it; if the wound is too large, cover only the area where the enema can enter, and if the pus-filled abscess is above, cover it more below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bow is in perfect position, do not allow flesh to fill it in; and if you cannot cover the breast with what you see, prepare it in such a manner that the bow runs as low as it can go, for when the bow is perfect, do not allow flesh to fill it in and if you cannot cover the breast with what you see, prepare it in such a manner: that the bow runs lightly downward, and leave nothing of the bow; and take consolidative medicines to place over the sound part, and keep them under a linen drape that covers all the healthy area; then apply force towards the hole in the breast a little wider than the first, for apply ointment with wool according to the size of the hole, and put it on the hole in the sound part to lighten the bow, and do not remove the large drape outside until after many days once; and that which is under the hole in the breast, often remove to remove the bow, and know what flows from the bow, if it be venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in such a manner and you see the nature that stands above the hole in the sound part, know that the breasts have already come forth, and approach health; and then release the wound in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not affected.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds heal slowly due to their condition, and those who do the opposite. And if undigested food comes from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not affected; and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is far away, apply drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as anointing diafinity, for there is a large part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take diafinity ointment, make it with rose oil, and sprinkle with equal wine in substance; then let it infuse and use it; and if you do not have diafinity ointment, cook honey thickened, or mix mirbane, aloes, and frankincense, grind them on honey when it is heated; then apply a paste, place it on the breast, and sometimes administer long plantain roots, which are like flour of wheat and farro; and use simple or compound medicines: grind them, make powder, put on the honey as I said, and use it; and if the wound is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, know that the corruption is deep, affecting the bone, or hard limbs, or ligaments; so treat the fistula from this treatment, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Pain in the nail is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or foot, or by chance arises elsewhere; and when it grows old and one does not take care of it, it comes to the abscess chaus, and spreads and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance may reach all of it; and brings corrosion until it reaches the bone, causing painful inflammation, and the head of the finger becomes wide, and the color fades.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the wound does not heal, then you must cut away all the remaining flesh from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is much great help if the bone is sound and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses upon the flesh and begins to prick, and the blisters, then you must place a rag under the nail that keeps the flesh apart, and lifts it up, and cover that fine flesh gently and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cover it and treat forcefully, for as long as the bone decays, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone decayed, then cover it as described before, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is injured and swells up, and feels great pain, then you must first heal it; then cover the nail with a sharp spatule cut across, and watch that the cuts do not grow down to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, then put something on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain comes from the dislocation of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	the dislocation that arises in the hands of some men by chance is either all flesh or has part or it has bone, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or the birthplace is in any of our joints.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which arises in any of the joints of the hand does not move, and that which arises at the joint of the hand, by chance, does move; the size of that which is flesh is light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which arises at the root of the joint is grievous to treat: handle it with care.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which is born or must be done last, it is necessary that you cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The movements that come together in this way come either by birth, or suddenly from a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut this scar, so that it heals according to its natural form; then place between two moist cloths or pieces of wool soaked in rose oil, to prevent them from adhering; or you can place between two thin pieces of linen until they are sutured as is appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the burn comes to either of these with the palm, cut this scar as is appropriate.
des vils	of evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	his veins large enveloped full of surplus melancholic humours, which come from many members of the body; and more occur in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer to him once an evacuation of black bile, and then cure him with the basilicon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron cure is according to two methods: one is to cauterize and cut out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and let all the black blood flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this manner: first, immerse the leg in very hot water until the flesh becomes tender. Then, stretch the patient's leg from just below the knee to the part above the knee; next, make a cut in the vein on one side, or two sides, or three sides, using a broad incision. Then lift and let all the black blood flow out by hand from one end to the other, until as much blood is released as the patient can endure. Afterward, close the wound and instruct the patient to dye it with meat juices that contain black bile; then repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The removals of the stone are done in this manner: straighten the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it into a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and place a cloth over the vein from its length to the head of the knee, or below the ankle; then cut the skin at the inch, and brand the vein on both sides until it appears when pressed; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then put the reed under it until it rises from the skin, and then lower it to the inch gently, then place another cloth above three digits; then brand the skin over the vein until it appears, then lower it to the reed, as you have done before, and lower it to another inch, as you did first; then cut a new size, or more if you need them, then lower it, and cut at the digit of the foot, then pull and lower until the second size; then remove size by size until it comes out completely, then put; and if you cannot pull and raise it, then insert a needle with a very strong doubled thread under it, and tie and pull, and place reed under it, and turn your hand from side to side until it is gone; and keep it from knotting, for if it knots, it cannot be pulled or raised, and this comes harmfully to the patient; and when you have entirely removed it, put wet cloth soaked in wine and rose oil over the place of the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it in a twisted manner, but do not cut it completely; and draw it out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron tool used to cut the vein is curved, and you do not cut completely, so as not to cut the vein; it should be a large curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil that lacks moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in legs, and this happens due to corruption that comes from beneath the skin, as serpents and worms do, embedding themselves between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes into the leg a very great inflammation, then the loins change, and the veins begin to come out, as if they were a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the loins are open, you must wrap around a piece of lint one and a half yards to two yards, and the thread, and leave the lint hanging from the leg, and every time there is none at the end, you wrap it again with the lint and the thread; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remaining with it, but do not cut it at its root until it is fully out; for if you cut it, it will enter into the flesh and cause an abscess, putrefaction or swelling; because of which it must be treated little by little until completely removed. There are times when this vein, when treated, reaches five yards in length, or ten with one hand spanning about a foot, to me who received one from which it issued ten yards long, and when you cut it, you pull out one span or digit, and pierce it thoroughly so that all of it comes out; and empty the matter inside, and apply medicines preventing putrefaction any day, then cure it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes there are main veins present, and especially when they appear in the joint of the foot or ankle, and there comes much bruising, and from which sprout main veins; treat them as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	verses that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often affects cattle, and is a small verse that grows between skin and flesh, and moves up and down throughout the body, feeling well as it travels from limb to limb, causing the skin wherever it goes to become inflamed and burst; and it is nourished by putrefaction of certain humors, coming from worms, serpents, and intestinal worms or parasites; and doubt is cast on its malignity, for when it moves through the body and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one cannot stop where it goes: therefore, you must tie the limb above and below with a tight rope, then cut and drain it. If the pus is fully in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; the greater harm it does is that it can enter the eye, as we have said; if you see it coming or close to the eye, hold tightly below it with a strong cord, then cut and drain it. The patient must use cleansing of body from medicines soluble for the bad putrefied humors, and beware of meat causing infection through putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those whom I say this of.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, as if live silver when it is cut from one piece to another; the pain left that part and stuck in the shoulder, and then a little while later spread through the entire body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that it returned to her torso, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered much how it moved in this manner from member to member, for I had never seen this disease proceed in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.
