First, I wished very much that they could move the pain from their side to another place, but I did not wish it as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a cold body, and her veins were uncovered, and because the wind illnesses constrained appeared; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who have warm bodies and their veins are covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears as we have said, scrape off the surface and underneath hastily, and then wash away until that wind illness constrained at the place has gone; and cauterize the place. And if you do not see it with your eyes, treat it as those that drive wind illnesses, such as bitter pills, and snake root pills, and other similar ones.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various types, according to their shapes and the parts of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their types is that some have large points, small ones, hooked ones, and those fixed together; and some have two angles, while others have tongues, and some have pieces. And the one that falls into any limb does so in various ways: it may lodge in a principal member such as the brain, heart, liver, thorax, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into any part of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you about later, appear: then you must be careful about extracting this arrow, for death often follows in various conditions; and when none of these bad signs appear, and the arrow is not completely removed, you should extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and a syphagma, which is above the brain, ruptures, is when there is scotoma and solidity and edema in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and by chance this may be without force from the nostrils or ears; and by chance it affects speech and voice; and a discharge from the wound of moist white pus resembling a pulse, and similarly as if boiled meat; and if this sign appears to you, hold off on treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes or hits the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; by chance the arrow may move like a pulse, and brings black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that cannot be removed by plumage is that without bubbles of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and warms up.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow drops into the covering of the foot, it affects the small bones; it causes great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow drops into the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound with something undigested from the meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow drops into the belly, and in its jump nothing but hay comes out through the intestinal tract, it has no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and urine spurts out and flows, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as the hand and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the elbow and the thigh and the legs, and limbs similar to these, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you would do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into the nerve at the root of the neck: I tried it, and removed it from another side beneath the ear fat, and he was cured without difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out an arrow that fell into the grease of the eye beneath the paper, and the arrow was embedded, and could not be reached except by the point towards the wood, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, light as iron without ears; the patient recovered, and no bad accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and drew it out thoroughly, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew an arrow from the man, that was in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition at all; I incised the arrow, devised a method, drew it out forcefully, and he had no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a person who has an arrow that fell or pierced the back, and the wound was stitched; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor caused any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you see another person who has an arrow that fell into his face, and the wound was stitched; and remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow that struck a man of the king's court, who was hit among the straw, and it was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely covered. I was called to treat it after it fell three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I made it with all my subtle skill, and did not feel it; and he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed above the wound an ointment poultice digestive and antitoxic, because the eyes were swelling; and I saw the eye of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice by hand for days, and redressed the wound again, and the patient remained in such a state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day beneath his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine by hand for days while the wound was open, and tried it, feeling the tip of the arrow rotting at the site; then I continued to treat the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent; and passed well through three months, after which I healed the wound so thoroughly that I could use tongs to extract it from both sides, but it would not come out; then I continuously innovated and devised various tools, until I successfully extracted it with properly made tongs on one day, as described in the form at the end of this chapter.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeon judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it, and the wound was sown, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or have I told you about the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your cure on what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything; but master surgeons compare on very little matter, and on what is present and lacking, find nine operations, and nine instruments, for the removal of things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not enter into the limbs in two ways: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and that which enters through the place where it enters is an arrow penetrating the flesh, and does not enter even once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it be left until the flesh rots entirely, and the issue is alleviated; and likewise if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and change it each day; then it will come out, and if it does not come out, pierce through to all the subtle parts entirely, until the flesh inside is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the other conditions I have clearly stated for the patient: do not draw it out at all, but let it be until it is equalized after a few days, because if the arrow comes just to the septum, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for several days, then the device to remove it should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed by force, I administer tar internally as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body so that it cannot be seen, then seek it with your hand throughout the wound; and if you feel it, remove it with an appropriate instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein, then enlarge the wound; and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are parts of the arrowhead that it holds, remove the flesh embedded on both sides until you can grasp it, and then break or bend the parts of the arrowhead to facilitate its removal; and with great care, ensure you do not break the arrow, as this would make its extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it stay until the flesh between the bones is rotten, then remove it, for the extraction would be painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you do otherwise, apply what we have said about the treatment in this chapter; and beware of incising the nerve or the vein, and move skillfully to extract the arrow as soon as possible, either firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell on him, for that is the greatest help that can be given, and if you cannot do so, then position him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another direction, or where it opens anything of them, or the skin is swollen in such a way that one can see or feel it: cut there, as deep as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it: if it is now stuck.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it there, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is inside, push the whole shaft; and if the shaft falls, and you see that a thrust is needed, then use the hooked instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is stuck, then push the instrument with the point entering it, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary to cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or a fish or in the belly or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can reach it, then you may cut out; and guard against cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound if necessary; treat the wound until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to that of a bird's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are different sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the needle is also similar to that of a bird's feather, for piercing the tip of the arrow, as shown in its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for pressing and knowing this is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins from which we draw blood are thirty-one, of which sixteen are principal, namely: two jugulars which are behind the ears and called "herbech"; and the two arteries which are in the temples and visible; and the veins that are in the lacrimal glands of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that runs through the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two subclavian veins which are around the neck; and the two veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins through which we commonly bleed are as follows in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it lies on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the median vein is called "fascia", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein lies on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the flexor, and it is the one through which we bleed, which clearly appears over the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the basilic vein is the vein that lies between the auricular and annular veins, and it has two sinuses; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of them lies below the bend of the arm on the left side, and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nervosa" that is in the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The healing of veins that are behind the ears helps in purging old bile and in migraines; and the qualities of the healer, as I tell you, are that you reset the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck to a screw so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two loops hanging from the head: hold them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, prick; then take the lancette, and make a cut beneath the vein up to the bone, then raise your hand all along the vein upwards, and cut away both the skin and the vein thoroughly twice through, and let out the blood until you see it; then drain it and bind it until it is healed; and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for migraines that have been around long, solid, and frequent headaches, and to the body of tears of water in the eyes; and the qualities of this health are as I say: and it is that the patient feels his neck strained so much that the two veins clearly appear; and you feel a pulse under your thumb, then sign with your third finger; then lift the heart over the vein upwards to your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and the flap, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then form it well, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about them regarding their application and their extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein for diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for flushing; and its quality is such that the patient's collar is drawn out by twisting, until the vein becomes visible; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then release the patient's collar, and bind the vein until it is saneel, and only once the work is done or with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	In all ways, it is not fitting that the flames be too fierce; and apply the flame in a crosswise manner, for the bone is nearby, and by chance, the flame might break the bone when it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps them, and with headache, and redness, and the orbit in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their health are such that the patient draws his colt from it by twisting at any ligament, as before; then the savior, and let the salvation through the traverse, a little long of flame a little wide, for there is no part of flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks; then make flow of blood, as much as you need, and then tie with cotton, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein of the nose is good for water and strong poison, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the qualities of the health are such that the patient draws his colt by twisting at any ligament, then pulls his nose with your left hand, and take the subtle long flame, and stick it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well here, and the wound will begin to flow now; and do not go too perfectly, and make flow of blood according to your need, then tie it one night, for it is most easily restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sinews of the two glands help in the narrowing of the artery, and in the beginning of atherosclerosis, and much to diseases, and to petechiae, and to erosion, and to herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the sinew is that the patient draws his collar away from both sides, as we have said; and let the master be above the patient's head, and let the patient lie on the seat, then heal the vein along a long bit widely, then draw temperate blood, or as much as needed; then do another part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and compress all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke; and leave until morning, that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the sinews of the glands
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The veins of the lips above help in swelling in the mouth, and to the decay of gums, and cracks in the lips, and around the nose and between them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are such that it makes the patient sit facing you, and holds his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be known by their being black, and by having small black threads around them: cut both of them, and if you do not know them, and are in doubt, cut the largest from each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, for it is done in the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health above the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are above the tongue helps after the health of the cephalic vein, and it is in the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the uvea, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of this healer is that the patient's condition eases before your eyes in the sunlight, and it lifts the tongue, and you look beneath on each side a black vein: therefore, both are healthy, and do not proceed too much to perfection, for beneath them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the ear that are commonly healed are treated in two ways: either by pricking with a sharp fine needle or with a subtle olive oil as you have heard, and it is called "aniseed"; and they are large and subtle according to the size and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the martyr's flame is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has need to open veins full of thick blood and apparent, and contain large and turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle and pointed, and is for cleansing subtle veins, where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the lungs, and in the belly; and it is suitable for the physician to bleed his patient and to avoid the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and a bleeding continues, it must be stopped as I have said; and one should not prick with fire, but cut like a razor.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilique vein does not open clearly, it must be extracted, and another replaced; or you take any part of it, or make a new incision in its place: it will then open clearly; and cut with the fire like a razor, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the location of the vein, it must be thus that you extract the arm, touching the location until you feel the pulse; then mark the location with a pin or needle, and bind the arm, cutting the vein with fire like a razor; and beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see the area swelling, for this is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bulge up high as urine in a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that it is a vein of the artery: then hasten, and place your finger longwise, then withdraw your finger when the veins have stopped, for this often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move it the patient until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the veins are not stopped, and it pains you, and medicines are not at hand, cut the vein if it opens, for the head of the shoulder is withdrawn; stop the veins.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark from the fig tree, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it well just to the other day; if the veins are stopped, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stoppages are not grievous for many conditions of the small wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm during treatment to draw blood from above the hand and beneath the body, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and the patient must guard against the nerve underneath, and if pricked too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the health is damaged, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, you must anesthetize the vein with the instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps in drawing blood from the hand and aids the eyes; and it must be treated by pricking with an olive oil flame or a mirtin oil flame, for this is the most safe of all veins, as it does not have any nerve or artery underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In all ways, it is necessary to seek the lightest touch, and not harm anything if it must be done for the first time, and one recommences; and by chance, swelling occurs in some people's joints when it must be done for the first time, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about a wound is that it is not induced except to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; and the wound should be treated in one of the three veins: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should treat the wound at the beginning of prayers on bended knees, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one should treat the wound on the first or third day after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medicine that is administered for diseases has no fixed hour determined, but rather when need is of day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not fitting to give medicine to children up to fourteen years, nor to women carrying a fetus from four months up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Medicine should not be given to the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be medicated, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that they purge their intestines with a light enema, if they have retained much fluid, so that the veins do not attract from the intestines the superfluous putrid matter harmful to the principal limbs; and medicine should not be given to one who is too salty from meat, nor to those who are drunk to excess, nor to dropsies. And when war is undertaken to medicate after colic, passion, vomiting, belly discharge, and frequent sexual intercourse, labor, watching, and fasting, and those whose entire virtue, whether by arms or body; then the subtlety of the humors, if the vein is large due to meat, drink, and medicines, you may have the power to thin it. And between bath, if any such thing does not prevent it, to subtilize the blood, and medicate from the vein near the third toe as we have said; and keep that day free of work, of labor, and of lust, and similar things; and be bound and loosed, and let the sayer be higher than he who is being treated, and rub the arm two or three times, then slightly restrain the ligature above, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot properly take hold. And then rub the limb with your hands until the veins swell and you can feel them; then grease the sayer's flame with a bit of old oil, then place his thumb on that vein under the limb at the spot he wishes to medicate, ensuring the vein does not become engorged or fail to take.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as cords in the veins, and some that are full of windiness, such that when one applies fire, they retreat from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one belongs to those; and if one incises the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which one must be cautious about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein incised opens on the first attempt, that is good; but if not, one must incise again a little below or above quickly, where the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient feels better, let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter a bath, and then resume the incision if you wish to continue; and if the wound is small, or the vein is shallow and you doubt whether there is as much blood as you see, then apply fire directly to that opening; work quickly, before the limb becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swollen, do not begin healing it anew, and place a bit of oil jelly on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and makes the jelly that the oil becomes; thus administer the oil jelly in each wound that you heal the veins, to staunch the flow of blood; and similarly make tar and bowen from it when you put it on the limb; so subtlely does the blood separate when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, even when the wound is not cleansed more than that time or the opening of the vein is small, you should hasten, and place on the limb a wet sponge in water and salt a bit warm, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood from the vein has drained out. And if any black or green remains on the limb after some days, it does not harm it; and if you see it, place on it something of aloes or myrrh moistened in calamus juice, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance on the skin of the basilica: therefore place your hand there, and if you find it soft under the pressure of the hand, that is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not apply anything of what we have said, for fear it may cut into the artery; but dress it with a dry poultice to harden the wound, and then treat with other salves until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person's blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it large, let it flow until it becomes fine; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for one who is full and fat, and has need of blood extraction, that a larger wound be made, and let the flanges be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and make him heal little but often, and should heal him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is saved from haemorrhage and nerve compression, and is better than long or wide wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose body needs nourishment during healing, it is fitting to give them soft bread with pomegranate juice; if they are heated, let them bleed 3 or 4 times. And if they have a cold complexion, let them eat soft bread before healing in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it swells in the arm, after the discharge of much blood, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it swells and becomes sore in the arm, and has swollen before, when it is weakened by great swelling, it is fitting that he be allowed to swell a little and a little, according to the quantity of its virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if it swells in the arm after the first swelling, and he has a strong cor, he should swell seven hours after the first swelling, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if it swells in another place, he should swell on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and this causes fever; it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the hole until it closes up in the pampson; after you have rewarded all the conditions of healing, and place your hand on your pulse when it has healed, so that death does not come from the pampson; and this happens many times, when the healers are negligent; and it is not fitting when you see release the arm, and let blood a second time, and the hole is closed, that you press firmly upon it; nor if it is crooked, that you extend the arm hastily, for this would be bad; but let it alone until it has healed a second time; or you prick at the tip of the flame, until the one who is frozen reaches the circumference of the vein hole and comes out, and place on it a little salt moistened in water, and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not compress it until the abscess is pacified.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the need arises to treat the blood a second time, let it be done in that same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is treated in place of the vein in the hand because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of treating it is as follows: the patient should hold their hand in warm water until the veins become red; then tie it moderately so that the vein appears clearly. Now treat it through the vein, not by length or width; and make the punctures wide, and suture well close to the joint of the hand. If no blood can come out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; if it is in winter, do not hold the hand in warm water again because it should be used more in summer than in winter; and the treatment of this vein is safer than any other vein, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cure for the healing of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: stretch the hand, and put it in warm water until the veins are swollen, if one can see them; and if the vein is across, and you cover it entirely, do not harm anything; and do not go too long perfoming, for the nerve is underneath all entirely naked of flesh, and then put the hand in warm water again, if the skin is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as needed, put a piece of wool and salt on the vein to quickly seal it, and do this for each limb.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The cure for the vein in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse (likely referring to a hernia), and do everything as I have said for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the throat is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the lungs, retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its remedy are that the patient pours hot water on it, and rubs it over the vein until it swells, and ties it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot goes much fluid from the reins; therefore, apply the remedy to the larger vein or at the ankle where it moves well.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you remedy it on the foot, beware of the nerves beneath, and treat them as you would cut through them; let the flamed asbestos be ready.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound cannot issue from it, set the foot in the water, and let it well empty the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound needs it for the first time, begin again the second time a bit above, because the loam is salty; nor doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the sponge of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The loam of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its wound values for pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its wound is such that the patient enters the bath, and expels four doles above the ankle by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, you can sain it in all ways that you can, and by crossing; and it is best to cop it, for the loam is clear, and it is very responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, cleanse any vein that appears on the side or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let the bleeding continue as much as you see, and then untie the bandage, and place a cotton pad and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is performed in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and the suction performed by pricking and extracting blood is done at fourteen places on the body, of which one is placed entirely over the head; another is inserted into the neck; two are placed on both sides of the neck; one suction cup is below the chin; one is placed on both shoulders; one is placed above the armpits; and the other cups are placed between both arms and both legs. And this suction does not draw blood, but only small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because it weakens none of them as much as a vein from a puncture would; and it should not be administered with fire or without fire in any disease caused by excess, until the entire body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or for custom, we conduct it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between and in every time; for there are such who, when they need to bleed, have heavy head; and such who find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes; and such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and reek of blood; and there are such who dream, and see by night blood and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it is between the hours, we order to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sinews of the muscle help in the healing of the fracture of the head... that comes to them, and it should not be that this happens after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in the place of the sinew of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those who have a cold complexion, or who have chyltrary, for it does them much great harm; because of this it should not be used by those who watch, nor those who have cold illnesses of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often suffers from this, becomes more forgetful, and because of this, it is necessary to place the cupping slightly lower due to the fear of increased forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventosation on the neck is in the place of the sinew of the head and the basilica. Because of this, it is effective for narrowing of the pulse, for splitting the channel of the arm, and for immediate relief and fullness; and it should be applied only briefly, for if it is held too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind disorders affect the two ribs of the neck and cause pain in the head, eyes, and ears, and are located in the healthy part of the basilica; and you must instruct the patient to place his hand when he puts it on, not to compress the artery, and avoid hemorrhage.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wind disorders over the chin cause mouth diseases, and gum corruption, and similar diseases in the mouth; and are located in the healthy parts of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind disorders of the shoulders cause diseases that come from heat and filling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind disorders of the groins are as affected by three veins of the arm, because they receive blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to cut too deeply, for the flesh is bare of muscle, and one can feel nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping device placed on the buttock treats hemorrhoids from below and internal diseases, and it must be large, made of iron, well-treated; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and I make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cups for the legs cure openly, for they attract blood from the whole body, and are effective for old pains in the kidneys, liver, and bladder, and diminish tumors; and they are placed on the inner and outer ankles, and generally weaken the body after long use, and bring about paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping device is as follows: first, ensure it is empty and thoroughly warmed, then place it hastily, and move it evenly without stopping until you see the skin turn red and swollen, indicating the blood's appearance. Then remove it, put on the cups again, and pay attention to the condition of the body, for some have thick flesh and clear pores: in such cases, only need to prick once, creating large wounds but not too deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it must be pierced twice: the first time to dilate the path of the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it must be pierced three times; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we need to dilate it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we must begin often; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it thoroughly, and the ends are such that the vessels are cut suddenly, and for those with thick skin and hardness, and who have small pores, you should anoint the eyes of the suction cups with a pungent and dissolving oil: if it is in heat, use olive oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in cold, use mustard oil, or lavender oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar oils.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take ambergris oil, or balsamite oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is being healed has flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to put oil, but he should be washed after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or pear water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from juniper, or cedar water, or myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large excesses rise from old wine, or decoction of safflower, or infusion of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not appropriate to heal with suction cups before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two. And do not sleep after ventilation, and he must be warm when he should be suctioned and when he is suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch that one who is healing and is choleric, and if the blood is too acrid and inflamed; it must take cold things, as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at mealtime, and similar things; and eats grubs, and flesh of castrated animals, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, must take syrop of honey, and moderate fragrant wine between evening and morning, and eats little, and eats grubs and small birds and pigeon; and on the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men treacle or mace before or after cupping to strengthen the principal members; and let the blood be diluted, but it must not be given to those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and mouth and veins and hip, for these limbs do not tolerate being pierced at their roots, and fire is made use of only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place them on the nipples when a child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place suction cups on the belly and mouth to alleviate the limb; and removes pain, when there is inflammation or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue incidentally the inflammation, or dislodges the stone from its place; thus does it when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suckle only; sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes filled with tepid water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a manner one fills the suction cup with warm boiled water or water with certain herbs cooked in it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two inches wide and half a palm in depth, and have or make a small hole in the middle to insert a needle, as for piercing an acupuncture point, and may it be made of tin, with the mouth open so that the patient does not become cold when placed on the limb; and have in the middle a cross bar of tin or iron to hold a wick, and let there be both large and small ones according to the diseases and the sensitivity of those who use them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, and of thin people from those of fat people.
