Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one should place this suction cup on the limb: take the wax or resin wick, and insert it into the suction cup through the cross bar that is in the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup and does not burn the patient; then put it on the limb, and let your two fingers be on the hole as we have said, so that when you want to, the vapor goes out, and remove the suction cup; and immediately insert the wick as before, and do this often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is applied in diseases of the pleura, for all acute conditions, it has neither a peg nor holes, and is not applied forcefully unless it is filled with fluid, and is placed only on the limb; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suction cups are not applied forcefully only in places where it is impossible to place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and on naked flesh, such as the palms or soles, and others like them; and the quality of the user is that when you find suction cups that are in clear, sweet water without corruption, take them; and put one nut in sweet water until they become accustomed and have nothing in their centers; and then bleed by vein and suction cup, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and place the suction cups on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where you can put a suction cup, apply one, for this is very useful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not so, lift the arm from the armpit, and then with water, very well, and then press it out; and if the arm is too swollen after the body's veins, make a cold linen bandage, and put it on until the flesh is infected; and if there are many abscesses, put broken vitriol or garlic, and similar things, until they are infected; or you put on half of peeled beans, and let them remain until they dry out at the arm, and will now stop bleeding.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the abscesses do not will to take, rub the arm with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the abscess flows out, and then put bandages on it. As soon as they smell the blood, they will dry out; and when you see that they are beginning to heal, sprinkle a little aloes and powdered salt or ashes on them, and they will now start to heal.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear friend, that the knowledge in this chapter did not appear in any of the ancient books or letters; and for this reason, the science has been lost in our land. For I found nothing good in it; and I know nothing of it except through the science of ancient books, in which I studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life. And I have described here what is contained, abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must state in the prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where the wise ones place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twists or sprains come to any person, it is necessary for you to hasten to heal the patient from both sides, if nothing else constrains you, such as bodily weakness, illness, or age; or if his hand is either too cold or too hot; and let him consume cold herbs, that is, cold jujubes, and meat of bird and chervil, and drink no wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not overeat food that fills the veins with blood until you have doubt of a hot abscess or the spreading of matter in the limb; so the patient returns to sound prior governance he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it must be nourished with meats that promote good healing or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, meat of fowl, oysters, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And in good nourishment, the healing is shown and the fractures are healed more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones in the old and decrepit cannot heal or set well according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset over the broken bone with strong tendons which will connect the limb together, so long as it enforces itself as it was before; and do not let it set completely from its work, and for this reason, you must nourish with good meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go across, and others that occur obliquely, just like the cuts of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place. And the fracture of the bone is known by the twisting of the limb, and clearly by palpation and by touching; and when there is no twisting or pain on touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there may be no fracture; but it can well have a twist, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit you to move it by hand, but place medicines that follow here, and then hold now delicately.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break going in an arc, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now put them together equally, as with abscesses that come to head; and if yellow abscesses come, let it remain a day, until the abscesses be calmed; then set it equal to the bone that you can lightly and safely touch, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold as follows hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, set them from two parts, if it is a hand or foot, or by your hand if it is a small limb, or by two strings, or one string and by your hand; and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you reduce all additions in their places on the bone that you can, and guard that through your work there come no injury nor pain to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if it seems not quite right: dress it beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly or press it as those who bring about a hot abscess and contraction to the limb through their work, as we have often wished.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at point, well chastise the patient so he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and see to it that the limb be so secured that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet at point, and it must be put in proper disposition so that no pain is felt; and take care that it be set straight, so that twists do not occur when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For it is that small limbs, such as arms and thighs and similar: it must be wrapped in soft, fine linen; and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg: they must be wrapped in a wide, firm bandage, for the wide bandages encircle all of the large limb and constrain it equally, so there is no gap; then tie over with light stops, three or four times according to the limb, and gently tighten your hand around the entire bandage, then go above the break and constrain less, that the break may move a little away from the break; and soften the bandage little by little, until you perceive a large part of the healthy area, then take the other bandage, and wrap again over the broken area; then return to the part below the break, and constrain moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first hour above; then place stops of linen or cloth evenly, so they are all equal, then tie everything over the bandage, and put your well-made pads on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something that cools and alleviates the abscess, and allows it to subside for a few days; then strip away the outer layers, which should be half as wide as a large cane reed, or from wood used for making splints, or palm ribs, and cut them according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it must be that the strips which one puts on the fracture are a little wider and larger than the others; and should be as long as is necessary for the size or length of the limb. Then bind over the strips just as you did at the first application, then tie over with a suitable thread, just as in the first application over the fracture. The threads must be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax. For if the threads are too thick, like those from leaves that make their bindings with twisted linen cord, this is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each strip.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the heads of arrows after the closure in their healthy places, then place lint or a linen bandage over them so that they do not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is burned and the tendons are broken, I will describe the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to extract arrows from all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to insert arrows forcefully on the first day; rather, do so after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your judgment of an acute abscess developing. And see here the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture not too thin nor too thick. This is the common way of using such a plaster to restore fractures in many conditions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster to restore fractures and dislocations and twists: take 3 ounces of bryony and mandrake and hellebore and asafetida and arabic gum and mugwort, 10; myrrh and frankincense, 5; aloes, 9; make them into a powder, and mix with honey from an egg; if the person's complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for twists: take mugwort and wormwood, 10; myrrh and aloes, 9; amber, 6; armeniac bark, 10; grind well, and mix with water or honey from an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method for plasters on joints and bones severed from their places, and alleviates the pain that comes with it, as well as the cutting of the bone, and the breaking: take new wool, and mix fat from swine and cooked oil, and apply to the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for alleviating hot abscesses, and properly removes pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for making a plaster to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for making a plaster to heal bone fractures and to reduce the swelling of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of visvalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vetches; of each part one; grind them and mix with wine; if the members are heated, mix with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster stronger than the first, when an abscess hardens during the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of visvalve, and seeds of flax, centaury, chamomile, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile; of each take one part; grind them and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras stated in his book that one should not apply anything on the broken limb to restore strength that cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he said it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should apply on the broken limb things dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another plaster useful for injury and pain: take mallow and hemp from combed flax, or bird feathers, and vinegar, and salt, and grind them together, and make a plaster of it and apply it where needed.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove it after some time, and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has moved the bone from its place; do not remove it with your hands just yet. If pain comes to the area, or itching, with no relief or swelling, hasten, and remove it, and take off the plaster now; and use a light cloth and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and apply it to the area as long as the itching ceases and the pain is appeased. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it tightly enough until you are sure of the warm abscess; and subdue the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the fine binding and a little plaster, but do not tie it as tightly as before; and continue this subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has become empty and redness and pain and swelling have all been removed, and you need to apply a plaster and bandage, then renew it as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of what we have said comes to the member, and it is not dislocated after three or four or five or seven days; and once in a while let it remain for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the broken ends harden and approach the setting of the bone; then restrain it more than at first, and allow it to grow its flesh as I said before; and if you see that the place is drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; immerse the wound in hot water several times when you dislocate it, and let it dry a little each third day; by this work therefore cut off the nourishment to the member, and mend hastily what the foolish menders do, which leave the member crooked: that is bad, and such works are fearful, and I see nothing else but letting and properly working on it.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Of various ways of breaking, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are breaks made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck fractures all the bone just beneath the bone, as does a hedgehog or a club; and because of this, this way of breaking is called "hedgehog" or "club.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this way of breaking is called "absolute"; it includes wounds from these two kinds of breaks, large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a compressed percussion, or a fracture of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar ones.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture close enough to the tissue beneath the bone, or upon the bone itself, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as finely as hairs, and the crack is small, and because of this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound made by striking with a stone, or falling, or similar thing, causes a piece of bone to enter downward, and the swelling of the hairs is like those of a smith when he strikes on cauldrons; so the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or chief moist bones, as in children; and it happens in all these kinds of fracture where small pieces are dislodged like stars; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all manner of breaks through their subtraction, and by examination with tests, and through the corrupt flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known by this: when the bone is discovered and rubbed over it, the black breaks become apparent.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient's condition. If you see any harmful symptoms such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, extension, paralysis, fever, and the eyes becoming protruded and red, and other similar symptoms due to various conditions, it may not heal with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the pain comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the moon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone becomes corrupt, and the accidents that we have said come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes just to the tissue that covers the brain, then it is fitting that you split the fractured part in such a way: and you must take hold of the end of the injured patient's head, and uncover above the bone in all the ways you can, and more so over the figure of the wound. And if bleeding from the bone comes with uncovering the bone, or an abscess is formed, then aid as necessary, and it is that you fill the space with moistened cloths in olive oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are pacified, and you are assured of no further bleeding; then begin splitting the bone to remove, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut precisely at the front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then we cut another larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron rod; and work lightly, so as not to blister the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, you must pierce it through and through, as when making incisions with trephines, not fully but so that the point does not pass beyond the bone of the skull, and should have a margin or circle above the point, preventing it from passing beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each comes to its place in the thickness of the bone, and you should have trephines for all skulls; and this is the form of the three kinds of trephines.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the broken bone are that you place the probe on the bone, and turn it to your two sides until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the probe a little bit to another part, and do this all around, then cut between the pertu with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the punctures, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools you have such as tongs, forceps; and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the sinew.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the displacement which has remained from the bone to all other similar instruments, but it must be more tense and more subtle than the other incisors; and if there remains nothing of the small bones or any scales, you should remove them gently with the tools; then treat the wound with powders and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galien said, who describes it as more simple; and he speaks very forcefully, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break has opened wide, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this incisor a lens-like object, the form of which is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and let the damaged part be on two sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently crack the bone all around, and take great care of the membrane beneath; if it is rough against the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed very harmfully and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then you must scrape beyond that roughness and remove the scales with a fine razor, in which you should have various quantities, to apply the most suitable part in each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you start with large razors and then use finer ones, and continue until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other small incisions and subtle fractures, you must apply the remedy according to its nature; and this is something that is not covered by him who devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the face is uncovered, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and ointment in rose oil, and apply it to the wound; then take another doubled cloth two or three times over, and ointment in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not burden the face, then administer above the other ligature, and do not strain it too much that it touches the wound only; and leave it for one or two days, until the abscesses are calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, mustard flour, incense powder, aromatic, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and apply it to the wound, and administer above it unguents without mordanting; and guard that the wound is kept clean, that you do not leave ointment, nor allow fluid to congeal on the brain fabric, for when liquid congeals on the head cloth, it runs down and causes great harm to the patient; for when one puts something biting on the face, nerves are affected above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take note, if no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if night comes only because of the medicine we have put on, that it has virtue, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and in gum one rag, and lay it on the sore; then cure it in the manner of cures that it should be healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts above the neck are broken, or only one of them, for these are two bones; and the one beneath is cartilaginous, and neither breaks nor causes pain by bending or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you place your little finger or thumb from the newborn on the equal part of the break and fit it into your index finger, and into the pocket behind it, so that the break regains its natural figure; and do this gently, and see that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose and your finger cannot reach the place, it is fitting that you put it equal to the end of a slightly thickened finger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is on both sides, do the same to the other side, and hasten to restore the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are healed, then place your finger at the end of the nose with linen threads, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you place it from another side, where the break is; let the tents be so large that they fill the pores of the navel.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And any restorer says that we should moisten the tents with butter and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is very good, but the tents should be moistened with a preparation of egg white and flour of wheat; then leave the tent on until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes place goose quills in the wound instead of tents, and cover with a dressing, and if the break is severe, let the patient blow through it; do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form on the nose while you are working on it, apply a cloth or a moist cotton pad in rose oil, or with a little iodine.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess forms on the nose, apply a poultice from above, made of silkworm silk powder and incense powder, cooked with egg yolk. Then place light stoppers on it, and do not bind the nose; and if the nasal fracture is small and broken into small pieces, extract it using suitable instruments, then stitch the wound and treat the tissue and bones with appropriate poultices and ointments. And if there are no wounds inside the nose, treat it with linseed compresses until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is ruptured but there is no wound, and the break is open merely, not shattered into pieces, but rather cleft internally, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is in the right part of the jaw, you should place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is in the left mandible, you should use your right hand to gently insert your index finger into the break, and close it with the other hand by pressing from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is separated into two parts, you should apply extensions to both parts, making them equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs or a rupture, strain them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place a dressing on the broken jaw and put a double bandage over it; place on this one a well-made pad or a piece of leather equal in size to the jaw, and attach it securely. Instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, release it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; apply a plaster with powder from the mill mixed with abundant egg or sinew flour after you have removed the dressing; put light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster dries out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses form, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward any fragment of the bone that has been removed; so subtle in removing with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with flamed irons according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these fragments, and there remains none, close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters over it to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the forcele
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder is fractured many times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is of three kinds: either it is broken and separated into two parts, with one piece, which is the easiest to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is as follows when the fracture has no wound: you should have two assistants, one holding the shoulder that feels the fractured bone, and the other extending the arm toward the proper part; then place the fracture evenly between your two hands so that the shape is as it should be, with neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place a round pad of cloth or wool over the shoulder on the patient; make it as large as necessary. Then gently lift and support the shoulder, holding the pad with your hand so that you can place the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder downward, because it comes from the front, then it is necessary for the patient to lie often on his side, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and order the attendants to lower the shoulder, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then attend to the break with your fingers, and if you find fragments, you must split them; and draw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join for any protrusion, then use one of your incisors; but place this instrument under the shoulder to prevent it from shifting.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not misplaced, and should be as wide as it suits, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the rupture of the wound you made when drawing the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, drain the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with bandages and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess is hot and swollen, I wrap it in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is felt due to wounds or cuts, is that you place on the bone a plaster of flour and egg powder, and put light bandages over it, and place a sphere under the splint if needed; then take a very wide cloth about a palm in width, and place the folded cloth over the bandage, and apply the plaster; next, take a thin stick about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that cloth, so that the ends of the cloth hang out; and place the stick on the splintered area, and turn the cloth up to the neck, under the splint, and over the healthy part, and the injured part; and bind each part well, and when you see that the ligatures hold the splintered area properly, and clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then reward each day, and when the ligatures loosen, release them; and have the injured lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the splint to raise the shoulder; this will alleviate the force of the injury by the support of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it until any bad accidents occur, up to twenty days; then reapply the plaster if needed, and bind and leave it as such until it is restored; and it is restored within twenty-eight days in most cases, and sooner for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When it comes to the breaking of the shoulder or large bone, and neither side is broken in the middle, nor is it out of place due to external force; adjust the joint according to the figure of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in all ways you can; then apply powder of the mill with abundant egg, wrapped lightly, and place a double flag over it. Next, put on a broad and thin strap slightly wider than the shoulder, ensuring there are no movements anywhere in the shoulder. If necessary, use linen stoppers to secure it evenly; then tightly bind it with a large bandage so that the strap does not move from its place, and check the ligament each day; whenever it swells, rebind it, and adjust the strap if it is out of position, and have the patient lie on their side. The shoulder will be healed in twenty or twenty-five days. When these numbers are completed, release it, for it is not bone that can be set lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone tends forward and out of the shoulder, cut it off, and do what we have said in breaking the collarbone to treat a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from breaking the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is broken in the middle only sometimes, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends outward, and the patient feels great pain, as well as swelling. Immediately, and by accident, they may vomit blood, and the movement in the broken bones becomes obvious, and everyone can see it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that when the patient lies on their back, place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs at your hands, carefully making all parts equal so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply poultices and ointments above the fine saline or other light substance, and wrap them in a cloth, securing them over the broken bone so they do not move. Twist the bandage round the back, adjust it appropriately, and rewrap it every hour; if it becomes loose, tighten it. If it is necessary to loosen it due to corrosion or itching at the site, pain, or an abscess, act quickly, loosen it, remove the poultice, and treat the area as in regular healing; then replace the bandage and keep it tight until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The breaking of the ribs comes from force applied behind the shoulder and at the back, and they bend due to their gappiness; and one feels this well upon examination along the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The resetting is that you align the break as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is turning inward, the patient feels intense pain and puncture-like sensations, similar to those from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the tissue; it causes spasms, and immediately vomits large amounts of blood, which is a serious health issue. The elderly have had to use great skill in treating this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is fitting to give foods that swell the belly to administer, to expel the burning sensation.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make such incisions that abscesses form if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that we should apply suction cups to the shoulder to draw out the swelling, and this seems reasonable. However, there is doubt that the suction cup will attract the superfluous fluids to the shoulder due to the weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that we should cover the shoulder with wetted wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the duration equal, then it should be treated with a pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone where the tendons are torn, and there is doubt for the patient, it is necessary to incise over the place of the broken rib, and one must put something under the instrument to guard against leakage; then one must cut the bone, and operate gently, and afterwards suture the two edges of the wound if it is large, and apply plaster dressings until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses continue to come up, put moist cloths in rose oil, and apply them to the rib; and treat continuously the rib as is fitting for an abscess, and let him lie on his side where it should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know whether they will be healed or not, if you see their hands softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they can move and feel well when you hold and prick them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient will recover if proper treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether they will be healed or not, if you see that the patches are softened, and if the accidents in the hands, and on the back due to wind and involuntary evacuation; and when one has sovined it over their belly, there is an involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is treated on its back and it wishes to heal, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is mortal: if it does not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply an espinea orroise (a spine from a rose) or oil from an egg if there is a hot abscess. Keep it applied until it calms down; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage. Instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is fractured, it must be treated on the heart; remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound, if large, with suturing, and apply an ointment promoting flesh growth until healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," you should hold your left hand's pouch with your right hand, placing it evenly within your reach, then put the plaster and bandage on, if needed; then bind it. If there are fractured bones, make an incision, remove them, and treat the wound until healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the hip bone is fractured, and if it is, there may be a slight alleviation at the head; make a long incision, and angle downward to the buttocks, and cause pain, swelling, and discoloration at the fracture site.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are on the wounding instrument; and know which are the wounds and their form; and if the wound is only on the head, so place an equal wound to it, as it be in natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the wound is long, or it declines inward, so lie the patient on their stomach, as the restoration of that wound matches you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it equally, apply a plaster, then place a stick or reed stake above, and bind the wounding instrument so that it does not move; and fill the area under the armpits, as the bandages should be equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his sound side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses begin to form, do not touch them until the abscesses are appeased, and apply what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and hold as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires are those between the scapula and the head of the shoulder. If they are broken, you must restore them according to one of the two methods: one method is that you take a stick of medium size, as shown in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two shoulders with two ligatures, and tighten them up high, and place the patient on the seat; then throw his broken arm onto the beam until it comes to the armpit, and have half a piece of wood in it, then place any heavy thing or the attendants above; then set the blades of the breaker equal with their hands together, so that the breaker returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that one supports the patient on his stretcher, and binds his hand to his neck, then commands two attendants that one hold what is on the breaker with their hands, and the other hold below the ligature, extending each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, tighten the ligature below the breaker and above it, and extend each of the attendants to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, it must be that you place the middle line over the axilla, and the other one toward the knife, under the break; and also if the break is opposite the knife, you must place the line lightly, without effort, until the break is equal on the bone and on the knife; then set the break equally as it should be, and bind it, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, you must not bind it tightly for seven days, and place a moistened piece of wool in oil on the axilla and in rose oil, until the abscesses are appeased; then bind it, and the way to bind it is that you apply the plaster over the break, then assemble the arm over the aid, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and bind over the aid and over the arm, so that the arm is in the position of stakes, unless any thing prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use wedges, and place one larger and stronger wedge on either side of the fracture, with two finger-widths of space between each wedge, making sure each wedge is large enough to span three finger-widths on both sides; then pry with the wedges as I said at the beginning of this chapter regarding the fracture, more forcefully but not by pulling apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the wedges and the tightness, as we have said, in the hour that you reduce the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is hot, let it remain until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine each three days the healing, to ensure there is no itching or swelling at the site, or that new growths do not appear on the limb because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the remedy, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents happen, and the dislocation is not reduced after three days or more, let the patient sleep on his back, and place his hands on his stomach; put under the shoulder a cushion filled with evenly cut wool, and observe every hour during the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the tendons do not become软化; by the virtue of medicine, it will heal, and let him eat the meat we have mentioned before, in such a way that the meat be first tenderized; when it begins to heal, make it more substantial.
