And when the dislocations are out of place, the patients lie down, as we have said in that which concerns gilbositeit, and draw the thread above the leg of the sick properly, and also above the foot; then put two sticks, one at the head and the other at the foot, then insert the stick between the thighs of the sick in the form; and plant moist cloths around, so that it does not blister the sick, then stretch each minister towards him, and the irons place equally at his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	And if it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	And if not, put it on the table and press it as we have said in the gilbositeit, and let the patient lie on the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it must be quickly extend the affected leg as I have said; and place the palm of your hand on the crooked leg, then press with the other hand, and straighten downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is to the side, it must not be extended downwards or lifted from the ground, but should remain as if the hip were dislocated to the side, as we have said in our discussion of lying on two hips; and let it be supported by the thigh, with the ligament stretched as we have said before, and apply pressure at the joint with your hand. It will be proper when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster and a bandage, so that the hips do not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then release it and put the plaster on again; and if you see that they are equal, apply the bandage as before, and leave it for three days; then release it, and allow the hip to heal well, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee can be dislocated in three ways: namely, within and without, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are as follows: you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the thigh. If it does not rest against the thigh, know that it is dislocated. The restoration of all this is done by seating the patient upright and extending their leg if possible. Place your back against their thigh and place their foot on yours. Then grasp the knee with your palms and draw it between your hands. Have others extend the foot until the knee returns to its place. The sign is that the leg rests lightly against the thigh. Apply a plaster, and heat the leg to the thigh, binding them tightly for three or four days. Then release the bindings. Do not allow the patient to move much while the limb is being strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle is sometimes injured, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and protrudes before the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is slight, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only injured.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must seat the patient upright, and hold the ministers firm by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot toward your right hand, and twice to the left, then extend it upward, and beautifully place the foot upward; do this twice, as we have said, by pulling and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, seat the patient on their back on the ground, and drive the stake firmly into the ground between their thighs, securing it with bandages tightly around, so as not to move the patient; then hold the ministers' thigh, and others extend the foot by their hands or by the ligature above the ankle; then extend each minister equally, and the stake should be fixed between the patient's thighs to keep them from moving when extending; then place the thumbs at the dislocation by the hand, and others hold the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at point, she puts the plaster and stops on it, and draws out the thorn, and binds the foot to the leg, and guards the nerves that are above the ankle behind, that the ligatures be not too tight; then lets it for two or three days, and if the ligatures soften, she loosens them; then unbinds at the third day or fourth, and keeps the patient from walking for four days; and if he goes before that termine, it is not safety that he does not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses chase away, it is necessary that you soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	Of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be beautifully extended with effort, and this is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any notch of the back or foot, you should seat the patient on a firm bench or on a table upright, and place his foot on what appears from these joints, then press strongly on his foot until it returns; and when it is equal, and there is nothing apparent, place under the sole of the foot a two-shouldered table, then hold firmly, and let him rest for three days, then release him; and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	for wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and you see it healing, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not long used it, and if you are not all wise and merciful and slow; but use at the beginning soothing things for the hot abscess, and leave the patient to God if you see no hope of recovery; and when you see hope, now reset the member to its place as the abscess cools down; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things for the cooling abscess, and cure the wound as it should be with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture with small broken bones, extract them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard against entering the way of fear according to what I have said, for this will avail you much according to your Creator, and for the wisdom that arms and protects you.
Amen	Amen
